class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="reproductive-health">REPRODUCTIVE HEALTH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reproductive-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unit-one-content">Unit one Content..<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-one-content" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Topic one: Standards of Reproductive health care in Kenya, Policies and initiatives related to Reproductive Health</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition-of-terms">Definition of terms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition-of-terms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Reproductive Health is a state of complete physical, mental, emotional, and social well-being, and not merely the absence of disease or infirmity, in all matters relating to the reproductive system and its functions and processes.</li>
<li>Reproductive Health Care is the appropriate constellation of methods, technologies and services that will ensure reproductive health and well-being by preventing and solving problems related to human reproduction and sexuality.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="basic-elements-in-reproductive-health">Basic Elements in Reproductive Health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#basic-elements-in-reproductive-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Ability - to reproduce, regulate fertility and enjoy healthy relationships</li>
<li>Success - result in child survival, growth and health development</li>
<li>Safety - Fertility regulation, pregnancy and child health</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="components-of-reproductive-health">Components of Reproductive Health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#components-of-reproductive-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th style="text-align: center;">o</th><th style="text-align: center;">Family Planning</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td style="text-align: center;">o</td><td style="text-align: center;">Safe motherhood (Maternal and Newborn Health)</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: center;">o</td><td style="text-align: center;">Management of STIs/RTIs and HIV/AIDS</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: center;">o</td><td style="text-align: center;">Promotion of Adolescent and Youth Sexual and Reproductive</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: center;"></td><td style="text-align: center;">Health</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: center;">o</td><td style="text-align: center;">Management of Infertility</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: center;">o</td><td style="text-align: center;">Gender Issues, Sexual and Reproductive Rights</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: center;">o</td><td style="text-align: center;">Reproductive Health Research</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: center;">o</td><td style="text-align: center;">Monitoring and Evaluation</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: center;">o</td><td style="text-align: center;">Community Reproductive Health</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: center;">o</td><td style="text-align: center;">Reproductive Tract Cancers</td></tr><tr><td style="text-align: center;">o</td><td style="text-align: center;">Reproductive Needs of the Elderly (Andropause/Menopause)</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Significance of Studying RH
o Reproductive health is a right
o Lead a responsible and satisfied sex life.</p>
<p>o To reproduce and freedom to decide when and how often to do so</p>
<p>o To be informed about advantages, possible risks and side effects of contraceptives</p>
<p>o To have free, equal access to safe, effective, affordable, and acceptable method of fertility regulation.</p>
<p>o To get access to appropriate health service of good quality to go through safe pregnancy and child</p>
<ul>
<li>Kenya has made steady progress in improving reproductive, maternal and child health outcomes in the last decade.</li>
<li>Child mortality has declined by over 20 percent since 2008 and the country achieved a total fertility rate of less than four.</li>
<li>Stunting, which remained stubbornly high over the past two decades has started to decline.</li>
<li>Six out of ten pregnant women now receive skilled care at child birth and over half receive postnatal care</li>
<li>However, despite this progress, Kenya could not achieve maternal and child health Millennium Development Goals (MDGs).</li>
<li>In Kenya today, many women, neonates, children, and adolescents continue to experience morbidity or die from preventable conditions that have proven and cost-effective interventions.</li>
<li>Access to quality Reproductive Maternal Newborn Child and Adolescent Health (RMNCAH) services remains a challenge across all levels of care, and inequities continue to persist among population sub-groups, and between rich and the poor.</li>
<li>The key supply side challenges include:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>sub-optimal functioning of the health system with uneven distribution of the health workforce as well as constraints in competency and motivation of the health care providers to provide quality care;</li>
<li>insufficient financing and weak supply chain management resulting in missing critical inputs required for service delivery, especially essential commodities; and</li>
<li>poor quality and utilization of routine data for evidence-based decision making.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Sociocultural and economic barriers and constraints in physical access to health services continue to limit demand
o Globally, there is also a renewed momentum and support for RMNCAH as part of the Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs) and the updated Global Strategy for Women's Children's and Adolescent's Health (2016-2030) which aims to achieve the highest attainable standard of health for all women, children and adolescents, and ensures that every newborn, mother and child not only survives, but thrives.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Such growing national and international commitments provide an opportune time to enhance both domestic and external support for RMNCAH in Kenya to ensure smart, scaled-up, and sustained financing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Improving coverage for RMNCAH services is a priority for the Government of Kenya as is reflected in its Vision 2030, the Constitution of 2010 and the Health Sector Strategic and Investment Plan 2014-18.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The Government has introduced new policies as well as initiatives such as Free Maternity Services, Elimination of User Fee for Primary Care and the Beyond Zero campaign to address the critical barriers.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="status-of-key-indicators">Status of Key Indicators<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#status-of-key-indicators" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maternal-mortality">Maternal Mortality<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maternal-mortality" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>"A maternal death is defined as the death of a woman while pregnant or within 42 days of termination of the pregnancy, irrespective of the duration and site of pregnancy, from any cause related to or aggravated by the pregnancy or its</li>
</ul>
<p>management, but not from accidental or incidental causes."</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-of-maternal-mortality-global">Causes of maternal mortality (Global)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-maternal-mortality-global" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251214-5944727f.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="direct-causes-of-maternal-mortality">Direct Causes of Maternal Mortality<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#direct-causes-of-maternal-mortality" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>These result from obstetric complications of pregnancy, labour and the puerperium and from interventions or any after effects of these events.</li>
<li>The Five major causes of direct maternal deaths in order of frequency are:</li>
</ul>
<p>0 Hemorrhage,
o Sepsis,
o Hypertensive disorders,
o Complications of abortion and
o obstructed labour</p>
<ul>
<li>Incidental/Coincidental causes</li>
<li>are deaths that were neither due to direct nor indirect obstetric causes. E.g. car accident, fire burn, bullet injury, etc.</li>
<li>Indirect Causes of Maternal Mortality</li>
<li>They result from previously existing disease or disease that develops during pregnancy which was not due to direct obstetric causes, but which was aggravated by physiologic effects of pregnancy.</li>
<li>These include:</li>
<li>o Malaria,</li>
<li>o HIV/AIDS</li>
<li>o Anemia.</li>
<li>Maternal Morbidity</li>
<li>For every woman who dies another 30 suffer long term injuries and illness due to pregnancy and childbirth related complications.</li>
<li>Maternal morbidity is any symptom or condition resulting from or made worse by pregnancy.</li>
<li>Severe maternal morbidity (Near Miss) is defined as: "any pregnant or recently delivered woman (within six weeks after termination of pregnancy or</li>
</ul>
<p>delivery), in whom immediate survival is threatened and who survives by chance or because of the hospital care she receives."</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-of-maternal-morbidity">Causes of Maternal Morbidity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-maternal-morbidity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Infection: There is high risk of infection of the genital organs (cervix, uterus, tubes, Ovaries and peritoneum) after prolonged labor.</li>
<li>Fistula: are holes in the birth canal that allow leakage from the urethra, bladder or rectum into the vagina. Women present with continuous leakage of urine or feces or both. The commonest cause in our country is obstructed labor as opposed to surgery and cancer in the developed world.</li>
<li>Incontinence: is involuntary leakage of urine.</li>
<li>Uterine prolapse: the falling or sliding of the uterus from its normal position into the vaginal canal. Commonest predisposing factors include prolonged labor, heavy exercise, multiple childbirths, etc.</li>
<li>Infertility: inability to become pregnant for a year despite unprotected sexual intercourse.</li>
<li>Nerve Damage: As a result of prolonged labor, there may be compression or damage of the nerves in the pelvis (Sciatic nerve) may result in foot drop and contractures.</li>
<li>Psychosocial problems: such as anxiety, depression, and psychosexual problem. Others Include pain during intercourse, low back pain, anemia, etc</li>
<li>Underlying Causes of Maternal &amp; Neonatal Mortality (The Three Delays)</li>
<li>There are three distinct levels of delay which contribute to maternal morbidity and mortality: (Thadaseus and Maine, 1994):</li>
<li>Delay in deciding to seek appropriate care. This could be due to: socio-cultural barriers, Failure to recognize danger signs, failure to perceive severity of illness, and cost considerations</li>
<li>Delay in reaching an appropriate health care facility. This is due to: long distance to a facility, poor condition of roads, lack of transportation and cost considerations</li>
<li>Delay in receiving adequate emergency care at the facility. This may be due to: Shortage of staff, supplies and basic equipment; unskilled personnel, user fees among others</li>
<li>Risk factors affecting maternal health</li>
<li>Socio-cultural factors: lack of literacy, early marriage, early childbirth, harmful traditional practices including female genital mutilation, etc.</li>
<li>Economy: Socio economic status affects women's status by affecting their decision- making roles in the community, educational status, health service accessibility, prostitution, etc.</li>
</ul>
<p>o Inadequate Health Service Coverage: More than 70% mothers do not get care during pregnancy and more than <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>90</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">90 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">90%</span></span></span></span></span> of deliveries are unattended. This can be due to lack of transportation, distance from health facilities, small number of health facilities, lack of knowledge about importance of health services, lack of money, and lack of family support
o Psychological factors: Fear of childbirth, too many pregnancies, death of other children illness in family. Women are at great risk of depression after sexual abuse, divorce as a result of marriage without consent and after Vesico-Vaginal/Recto- Vaginal fistula (VVF/RVF).
o Health and nutrition services: The health status of women who are not getting adequate nutrients and proper reproductive health services could be affected
o Interaction with providers: Some health care providers are not empathetic and caring. They do not respect women's cultural preferences for privacy, birth position, or the preference for treatment by women providers.
o Gender Discrimination: The family may give more attention to a male child with regard to education, nutrition; may want the mother to produce boys. Policy decisions, inheritance etc.</p>
<ul>
<li>Maternal Morbidity</li>
<li>For every woman who dies another 30 suffer long term injuries and illness due to pregnancy and childbirth related complications.</li>
<li>Maternal morbidity is any symptom or condition resulting from or made worse by pregnancy.</li>
<li>Severe maternal morbidity (Near Miss) is defined as: "any pregnant or recently delivered woman (within six weeks after termination of pregnancy or delivery), in whom immediate survival is threatened and who survives by chance or because of the hospital care she receives."</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-of-maternal-morbidity">Causes of Maternal Morbidity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-maternal-morbidity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Infection: There is high risk of infection of the genital organs (cervix, uterus, tubes, Ovaries and peritoneum) after prolonged labor.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fistula: are holes in the birth canal that allow leakage from the urethra, bladder or rectum into the vagina. Women present with continuous leakage of urine or feces or both. The commonest cause in our country is obstructed labor as opposed to surgery and cancer in the developed world.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Incontinence: is involuntary leakage of urine.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Uterine prolapse: the falling or sliding of the uterus from its normal position into the vaginal canal. Commonest predisposing factors include prolonged labor, heavy exercise, multiple childbirths, etc.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Infertility: inability to become pregnant for a year despite unprotected sexual intercourse.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nerve Damage: As a result of prolonged labor, there may be compression or damage of the nerves in the pelvis (Sciatic nerve) may result in foot drop and contractures.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Psychosocial problems: such as anxiety, depression, and psychosexual problem. Others Include pain during intercourse, low back pain, anemia, etc</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Underlying Causes of Maternal &amp; Neonatal Mortality (The Three Delays)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>There are three distinct levels of delay which contribute to maternal morbidity and mortality: (Thadaseus and Maine, 1994):</p>
</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>Delay in deciding to seek appropriate care. This could be due to: socio-cultural barriers, Failure to recognize danger signs, failure to perceive severity of illness, and cost considerations
Delay in reaching an appropriate health care facility. This is due to: long distance to a facility, poor condition of roads, lack of transportation and cost considerations
Delay in receiving adequate emergency care at the facility. This may be due to: Shortage of staff, supplies and basic equipment; unskilled personnel, user fees among others</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="risk-factors-affecting-maternal-health">- Risk factors affecting maternal health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors-affecting-maternal-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Socio-cultural factors: lack of literacy, early marriage, early childbirth, harmful traditional practices including female genital mutilation, etc.</li>
<li>Economy: Socio economic status affects women's status by affecting their decision- making roles in the community, educational status, health service accessibility, prostitution, etc.</li>
<li>Inadequate Health Service Coverage: More than 70% mothers do not get care during pregnancy and more than <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>90</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">90 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">90%</span></span></span></span></span> of deliveries are unattended. This can be due to lack of transportation, distance from health facilities, small number of health facilities, lack of knowledge about importance of health services, lack of money, and lack of family support</li>
<li>Psychological factors: Fear of childbirth, too many pregnancies, death of other children illness in family. Women are at great risk of depression after sexual abuse, divorce as a result of marriage without consent and after Vesico-Vaginal/Recto- Vaginal fistula (VVF/RVF).</li>
<li>Health and nutrition services: The health status of women who are not getting adequate nutrients and proper reproductive health services could be affected</li>
<li>Interaction with providers: Some health care providers are not empathetic and caring. They do not respect women's cultural preferences for privacy, birth position, or the preference for treatment by women providers.</li>
<li>Gender Discrimination: The family may give more attention to a male child with regard to education, nutrition; may want the mother to produce boys. Policy decisions, inheritance etc.</li>
</ul>
<p>The Kenya Maternal and Newborn Health (MNH) Pillars</p>
<ol>
<li>Family planning and pre-pregnancy care: To ensure that individuals and couples have the information and services to plan the timing, number and spacing of pregnancies.</li>
<li>Focused Antenatal Care - To prevent complications where possible and ensure that complications of pregnancy are detected early and treated appropriately.</li>
<li>Essential Obstetric Care - To ensure that essential care for the high-risk pregnancies and complications is made available to all women who need it.</li>
<li>Essential Newborn Care - To ensure that essential care is given to newborns from the time they are born up to 28 days in order to prevent complications that may arise after birth</li>
<li>Targeted Postpartum Care- To prevent any complication occurring after childbirth and ensure that both mother and baby are healthy and there is no transmission of infection from mother to child.</li>
<li>Post Abortion Care - to provide clinical treatment to all women and girls seeking care, for complications of incomplete abortion and miscarriage as well as counselling and contraceptives.
(Note that HIV services are now integrated into ALL the pillars of MNH and clean and safe delivery is part of Essential Obstetric Care)</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="skilled-attendance">Skilled Attendance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#skilled-attendance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Evidence has shown that there are 2 key interventions that improve maternal health and reduce maternal mortality, namely:</li>
<li>Skilled attendance at delivery (skills, numbers, enabling environment) and</li>
<li>availability of Emergency Obstetric Care.</li>
</ul>
<p>The term "skilled attendant" refers exclusively to people with midwifery skills (e.g. doctors, midwives, nurses, clinical officers) who have been trained to proficiency in the skills necessary to manage normal deliveries and diagnose or refer obstetric complications.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="enabling-environment">Enabling Environment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#enabling-environment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>To ensure effective and efficient service delivery, the skilled attendant requires an enabling environment.</li>
<li>There is need for appropriate infrastructure as well as ensuring that the continuum of care is connected by an effective referral system, and supported by adequate supplies, equipment, drugs, good management and supportive supervision.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="referral-systems">Referral Systems<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#referral-systems" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A key aspect in ensuring a good maternal health service is a functional referral system.</li>
<li>Access to a telephone and/or vehicle, with emergency funds or fuel to transfer urgent cases day or night is extremely important.</li>
<li>Good record keeping and use of detailed referral letters will assist in reducing delay in the care for women with obstetric emergencies and severely ill newborns.</li>
<li>The referring unit should be aware of the capacity of the referral point to manage the client being referred.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="community-action-partnerships">Community Action, Partnerships<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-action-partnerships" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Involving community members (particularly women and their families, health care providers, and local leaders) in efforts to improve maternal health helps to ensure programme success;</li>
<li>Community education about obstetric complications and when and where to seek medical care is important to ensure birth planning/ use of birth preparedness cards, early recognition of complications and prompt caretaking behaviour</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="male-involvement-and-participation">Male Involvement and Participation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#male-involvement-and-participation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>it is evident that for successful programme implementation, male participation in MNH results in good outcomes for both mother and baby.</li>
<li>Male involvement and participation is critical in addressing the first and second delay.</li>
<li>In the Kenyan context, men have the resources and are the main decision makers in the families and communities on issues relating to MNH.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="equity-for-all">Equity for All<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#equity-for-all" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Rights based perspective helps legitimize prioritization of women's health.</li>
<li>It focuses attention on social, economic and geographic inequities.</li>
<li>Strong political support and national ownership are essential to create enabling policies to attract resources for maternal and newborn health and to ensure those resources reach groups with the highest maternal mortality and morbidity.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reproductive-rights">Reproductive Rights<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reproductive-rights" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Health care providers should appreciate that most maternal and neonatal deaths are avoidable, and therefore maternal and newborn health must be given its due prominence.</li>
<li>Safe Motherhood is a basic human right as women are entitled to enjoy a safe pregnancy and childbirth.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="emergency-obstetric-care">Emergency Obstetric Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#emergency-obstetric-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Emergency Obstetric Care refers to a set of minimal health care elements, which should be availed to all women during pregnancy and delivery.</li>
<li>It includes both life-saving and emergency measures e.g. Caesarean section, manual removal of placenta, etc, as well as non-emergency measures (e.g. use of the partograph to monitor labour, active management of the third stage of labour, etc.).</li>
<li>Emergency Obstetric Care functions are generally categorized as Basic Emergency Obstetric Care (BEmOC) and Comprehensive Emergency Obstetric care (CEmOC).</li>
<li>Basic Emergency Obstetric Care Include:</li>
<li>Administration of IV antibiotics.</li>
<li>Administration of magnesium sulphate.</li>
<li>Administration of parental oxytocics.</li>
<li>Performing manual removal of the placenta.</li>
<li>Performing removal of retained products.</li>
<li>Performing assisted vaginal delivery (e.g. by vacuum extraction).</li>
<li>Performing newborn resuscitation</li>
<li>Comprehensive Emergency Obstetric Care</li>
<li>includes all the seven above, PLUS:</li>
<li>Performing surgery (Caesarean section), including provision of emergency obstetric anaesthesia.</li>
<li>Administration of blood transfusion.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="client-rights">Client Rights<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#client-rights" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Right to Information</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>All members of the community have a right to information on the benefits of reproductive health including Maternal and Newborn health for themselves and their families. They also have a right to information on how to access the services.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right to Access</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>All members of the community have a right to receive services from reproductive health / MNH programs, regardless of their socioeconomic status, political affiliations, religious beliefs, ethnic origin, marital status or geographical location. Access includes freedom from barriers such as policies, standards and practices, which are not scientifically justifiable.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right of choice</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Individuals and couples have the right to decide freely where to obtain RH /MNH services.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right to safety</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clients have a right to safety in the practice of MNH</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right to Privacy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clients have a right to privacy while holding conversation with service providers and while undergoing physical examination.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right to Confidentiality</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The client should be assured that any information she/he provides or any details of the service received will not be communicated to other parties without her/his consent.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right to Dignity</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reproductive Health /MNH clients have a right to be treated with courtesy, consideration, and attentiveness and with full respect of their dignity regardless of their level of education, social status or any other characteristics, which would single them out or make them vulnerable to abuse.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right to Comfort</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clients have a right to comfort when receiving services. This can be ensured by providing quality services in hygienically safe and conveniently located service delivery sites.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right to Continuity of Care</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clients have a right to receive services and reliable supply of RH /MNH commodities and drugs for as long as they need them.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Right of Opinion</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clients have a right to express their views freely on the services they receive.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Providers' Rights</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Training</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To continuously have access to the knowledge and skills needed to perform all the tasks required of them.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Information</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To be kept informed on issues related to their duties</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Infrastructure</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To have appropriate physical facilities and organization to provide services at an acceptable level of quality.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Supplies</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To receive continuous and reliable supplies and materials required for providing reproductive health services at acceptable standards of quality.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Guidance</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To receive clear, relevant and objective guidance.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Back up</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To be reassured that whatever the level of care at which they are working they will receive support from other individuals or units.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Respect</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To receive recognition of their competence and potential, and respect for their human needs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Encouragement</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To be given stimulus in the development of their potential, initiative and creativity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Feedback</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To receive feedback concerning their competence and attitudes as judged by others.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Self-expression</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To express their views freely, concerning the quality and efficiency of the reproductive health program.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="policies-and-initiatives-related-to-reproductive-health">Policies and initiatives related to Reproductive health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#policies-and-initiatives-related-to-reproductive-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-safe-motherhood-initiative-smi">THE SAFE MOTHERHOOD INITIATIVE (SMI)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-safe-motherhood-initiative-smi" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Safe motherhood is women's ability to have a safe and healthy pregnancy and delivery</li>
<li>The Global Safe Motherhood Initiative launched in Nairobi in 1987 aimed at reducing the burden of maternal deaths and ill health in developing countries.</li>
<li>The Safe Motherhood Initiative differed from other health initiatives in that it focused on the well-being of women as an end in itself.</li>
<li>In the SMI, the prevention of the death of a pregnant woman is considered to be the key objective, not because death adversely affects children and other family members but because women are intrinsically valuable (Thaddeus and Maine 1994).</li>
<li>It underscored the fact that Safe motherhood is a basic human right</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="summary-of-smi-events">Summary of SMI Events<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary-of-smi-events" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>International Conference for Population and Development (ICPD)</li>
<li>The 1994 International Conference on Population and Development in Cairo recommended to the international community a set of important population and development objectives.</li>
<li>The Programme of Action was striking for the attention it devoted to the issue of women's health.</li>
<li>It also included goals with regard to education, especially for girls, and for the further reduction of infant, child and maternal mortality levels.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="international-conference-for-population-and-development-icpd">International Conference For Population and Development (ICPD)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#international-conference-for-population-and-development-icpd" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>For Kenya, the ICPD recommendations were then translated into the National Reproductive Health Strategy (NRHS 1997 - 2010) and implementation plan whose goal was to reduce maternal, perinatal and neonatal morbidity and mortality.</li>
<li>Another event that followed the ICPD was the Millennium Declaration in 2000 and the development of goals (MDGs) with indicators.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="national-reproductive-health-policy-2007">National Reproductive Health Policy 2007<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#national-reproductive-health-policy-2007" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The goal of the RH policy is to enhance the Reproductive Health status of all Kenyans through:</li>
<li>Increased equitable access to RH services</li>
<li>Improved quality, efficiency and effectiveness of service delivery at all levels</li>
<li>Improved responsiveness to clients' needs</li>
<li>The main objective for Safe Motherhood in this RH Policy is to reduce maternal, peri-natal and neonatal morbidity and mortality in Kenya</li>
<li>The National Health Sector Strategic Plan (NHSSP II)-2005-2010</li>
<li>The aim of NHSSP II was to reverse the decline in the health status of Kenyans through an efficient, high quality health care system that is accessible, equitable and affordable for every Kenyan household.</li>
<li>A major feature of the NHSSP is the introduction of the Kenya Essential Package for Health (KEPH), which focuses on the health needs of individuals through the six stages of the human life cycle.</li>
<li>The strategic plan emphasizes strong community involvement in health care through the community Strategy</li>
<li>National Reproductive Health Strategy (NRHS): 2009- 2015</li>
<li>This is a revision of the NRHS 1997-2010 and includes issues and challenges that had not been incorporated in the original strategy.</li>
<li>The revision was also necessary in order to align it to the National RH Policy 2007.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-keph-life-cycle-cohorts">The KEPH Life-Cycle Cohorts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-keph-life-cycle-cohorts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>They are delineated in the NHSSP II as follows</li>
<li>o Cohort 1: -Pregnancy, delivery and the newborn child (up to 2 weeks of age)</li>
<li>o Cohort 2: - Early childhood (3 weeks to 5 years)</li>
<li>o Cohort 3: - Late childhood (6-12 years)</li>
<li>o Cohort 4: - Adolescence (13-24 years)</li>
<li>o Cohort 5: - Adulthood (25-59 years)</li>
<li>o Cohort 6: - Elderly (60 years and over)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="levels-of-care-in-keph">Levels of Care in KEPH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#levels-of-care-in-keph" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>â‹…</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\cdot</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">â‹…</span></span></span></span></span> The KEPH approach is not only limited to a definition of the target groups in terms of life-cycle cohorts.</li>
<li>It also defines where the health services will be delivered.</li>
<li>Under KEPH, promotive, preventive and curative services are provided at six levels of care:</li>
<li>Level 6 : tertiary hospitals</li>
<li>Level 5: secondary hospitals</li>
<li>Level 4: primary hospitals</li>
<li>Level 3: health centres, maternity, nursing homes</li>
<li>Level 2: dispensaries / clinics</li>
<li>Level 1:
villages/household/families/individ uals</li>
</ul>
<p>NB</p>
<ul>
<li>As a result of the implementation of the constitution of Kenya 2010, health functions have been devolved to the county.</li>
<li>In the structure, County Health Services are organized around three levels of care:</li>
<li>Community,</li>
<li>Primary care, and</li>
<li>Referral services.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="annual-operational-plans-aops">Annual Operational Plans (AOPs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#annual-operational-plans-aops" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The Annual Operational Plans (AOPs) translate Kenya Essential Package for Health and the National Health Sector Strategic Plan II 2005-2010 into 'actionable' operational plans.</li>
<li>AOPs also improve the planning process within the Ministry in particular highlighting the need for</li>
<li>Improved coordination and decision-making</li>
<li>Elimination of duplication of activities and</li>
<li>More efficient use of available resources</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-community-strategy">The Community Strategy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-community-strategy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The community-based approach, is the mechanism through which households and communities take an active role in health and health-related development issues.</li>
<li>Initiatives outlined in the approach target the major priority health and related problems affecting all cohorts of life at the community and household levels level 1 of the KEPH-defined service delivery.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vision-2030">Vision 2030<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vision-2030" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Kenya Vision 2030 is the country's new development blueprint covering the period 2008 to 2030.</li>
<li>The vision is based on three "pillars" namely;</li>
<li>o the economic pillar,</li>
<li>o the social pillar and</li>
<li>o the political pillar.</li>
<li>Health is part of the social pillar.</li>
<li>To improve the overall livelihoods of Kenyans, the country aims to provide an efficient and high-quality health care system with the best standards.</li>
<li>This is in order to reduce health inequalities and improve indicators in key areas where Kenya is lagging, especially in lowering infant and maternal mortality.</li>
<li>Specific strategies include:</li>
<li>o provision of a robust health infrastructure network;</li>
<li>o improving the quality of health service delivery to the highest standards and promotion of partnerships with the private sector.</li>
<li>In-addition the Government has put in place health financing mechanisms to make quality MNH services affordable and accessible to all especially the poor and vulnerable women.</li>
<li>These include the provision of free MNH /FP services at the lower levels, National Health Insurance Fund (NSSF), Health Sector Support Fund (HSSF), Hospital Management Support Fund (HMSF), FIF, Voucher system /Output Based Aid (OBA).</li>
<li>The government is also encouraging initiatives that promote communitybased health financing.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assignment-study-the-following-policies-initiatives">Assignment: study the following policies/initiatives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assignment-study-the-following-policies-initiatives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The Kenya Constitution (2010) calls for the highest attainable standard for health including reproductive health for all Kenyans</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The Kenya Health Policy (2014-30) commits to strengthening the health care system and service delivery.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Kenya Health Sector Strategic and Investment Plan (2014-18) (MOH 2014A, B, MOH 2012).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Free Maternity Care</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Elimination of User Fee for Public Primary Health Care Services,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Beyond Zero campaign.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Kenya RMNCAH investment framework</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Universal Health Coverage</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="millennium-development-goals-mdgs">Millennium Development Goals (MDGs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#millennium-development-goals-mdgs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>MDGs were set by all Government leaders at the UN Millennium Summit, September 2000)</li>
<li>All UN organisations decided to be guided by MDGs in their future action: unity of purpose, coherent action, synergies and strategic approaches by the UN system as a whole (guided by CEB)</li>
<li>Leaders pledged to strive, individually and collectively, towards these goals through international, regional and national action, concerted by the UN.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="why-the-mdgs">Why the MDGs?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#why-the-mdgs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The 1990s was a decade of faltering progress on:</li>
<li>Under-5 mortality rate</li>
<li>Maternal mortality rate</li>
<li>Child malnutrition</li>
<li>Water and sanitation</li>
<li>Income poverty</li>
<li>Primary education</li>
<li>MDGs were meant to accelerate progress</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="millennium-development-goals-mdgs">Millennium Development Goals (MDGs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#millennium-development-goals-mdgs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Goal 1. Eradicate extreme poverty and hunger
Goal 2. Achieve universal primary education
Goal 3. Promote gender equality and empower women
Goal 4. Reduce child mortality
Goal 5. Improve maternal health
Goal 6. Combat HIV/AIDS, malaria and other diseases
Goal 7. Ensure environmental sustainability</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mdgs-related-to-rh">MDGS related to RH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mdgs-related-to-rh" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Goal 3 Promote gender equality &amp; empower women
Goal 4 Reduce child mortality by 2015 the no at 1990
Goal 5 Improve maternal health</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="progress-of-mdgs-related-to-rh-2014-infant-mortality-rate">Progress of MDGs Related To RH 2014 Infant Mortality Rate<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#progress-of-mdgs-related-to-rh-2014-infant-mortality-rate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The KDHS 2014 shows a decrease in the infant mortality rate from 52 to 39 per 1,000 live births, and a decrease in the under-five mortality rate from 74 to 52 per 1,000 live births between 2008 and 2014.</li>
<li>These declines have been driven mainly by:
o o Enhanced use of mosquito nets,
o o Increases in antenatal care,
o o skilled attendance at childbirth,
o o Postnatal care,
o o Contraceptive use,
o o exclusive breastfeeding practices and
o o a decrease in unmet family planning (FP) needs,
o o as well as overall improvements in other social indicators such as education and access to water</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="neonatal-mortality-rate">Neonatal Mortality Rate<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#neonatal-mortality-rate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The NMR declined from 31 per 1,000 births to 22 per 1,000 live births between 2008-2014.</li>
<li>However, during the past decade, the NMR exhibited the slowest decline.</li>
<li>Further reductions in infant and child mortality require steeper decline in the NMR, which is closely linked to improvements in maternal health services including intrapartum care.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maternal-health">Maternal Health<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maternal-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The MMR of 362 per 100,000 live births estimated by KDHS in 2014 is still high</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Coverage/utilization indicators also show some improvements but much more needs to be done to address inequities and to reach Universal Health Care (UHC).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The contraceptive prevalence rate (CPR, any method) among married women has increased to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>58</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">58 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">58%</span></span></span></span></span> in 2014 from <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>46</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">46 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">46%</span></span></span></span></span> in 2008/9 with a decline in unmet need for FP.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nearly two thirds (61%) of births took place in a health facility and 62% of pregnant women were delivered by a skilled attendant.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Postnatal care (PNC) increased from 42% in 2009 to 51% in 2014</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The total fertility rate has declined from 4.6 in 2008/9 to 3.9 in 2014; however, there has been no change in teen pregnancy with one in five (18%) adolescents in the 15-19 years age group having started child bearing due to early marriage, high unmet need for contraception and poor access to FP services.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nutritional status of children under-five has improved with a decline in stunting from <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>35</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">35 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">35%</span></span></span></span></span> in 2008/9 to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>26</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">26 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">26%</span></span></span></span></span> in 2014.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>However, one out of every four children still remain shorter for their age, a factor that adversely affects their future health, well-being and economic productivity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nearly half (48%) of households have access to an insecticide treated net;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>53</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">53 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">53%</span></span></span></span></span> of women and <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>46</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">46 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">46%</span></span></span></span></span> of men were tested for HIV in the past 12 months and received the test results.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Overall immunization coverage for basic vaccines increased from 65.3 percent 2008/9 to 71.3 percent in 2014 and coverage for measles, pentavalent and pneumococcal vaccine remained high.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prevalence of exclusive breastfeeding among children under 6 months has nearly doubled from 32 percent to 61 percent</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sustainable-development-goals-sdgs-the-2030-agenda-for-sustainable-development">SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT GOALS (SDGs) - The 2030 Agenda for Sustainable Development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sustainable-development-goals-sdgs-the-2030-agenda-for-sustainable-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A set of 17 goals for the world's future, through 2030</li>
<li>Backed up by a set of 169 detailed Targets</li>
<li>Negotiated over a two-year period at the United Nations</li>
<li>Agreed to by nearly all the world's nations, on 25 Sept 2015</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sdgs">SDGs:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sdgs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>#1: End poverty in all its forms everywhere
#2: End hunger, achieve food security and improved nutrition and promote sustainable agriculture
#3: Ensure healthy lives and promote well-being for all at all ages
#4: Ensure inclusive and quality education for all and promote lifelong learning
#5: Achieve gender equality and empower women and girls</p>
<p>#6: Ensure access to water and sanitation for all
#7: Ensure access to affordable, reliable, sustainable and modern energy for all
#8: Promote inclusive and sustainable economic growth, employment and decent work for all
#9: Build resilient infrastructure, promote sustainable industrialization and foster innovation
#10: Reduce inequality within and among countries
#11: Make cities inclusive, safe, resilient and sustainable
#12: Ensure sustainable consumption and production patterns
#13: Take urgent action to combat climate change and its impacts*
#14: Conserve and sustainably use the oceans, seas and marine resources
#15: Sustainably manage forests, combat desertification, halt and reverse land degradation, halt biodiversity loss
#16: Promote justice, peaceful and inclusive societies
#17: Revitalize the global partnership for sustainable development</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="what-is-new-and-different-about-the-17-sdgs">What is New and Different about the 17 SDGs?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-new-and-different-about-the-17-sdgs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>These Goals apply to every nation ... and every sector. Cities, businesses, schools, organizations, all are challenged to act. This is called Universality</li>
<li>The Goals are all inter-connected, in a system. We cannot aim to achieve just one Goal. We must achieve them all. This is called Integration</li>
<li>Achieving these Goals involves making very big, fundamental changes in how we live on Earth. This is called Transformation</li>
<li>The vision is for the goals to promote sustainable development and poverty eradication.</li>
</ul>
<p>The first 16 goals address priority areas that:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>o Increase the ambition/ improving and sustaining current achievements on existing MDG goals (poverty, health education, gender) with added dimensions on</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>o Economic sustainability (inclusive growth, jobs, infrastructure, industrialization)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>o Environmental sustainability (climate change, oceans and land-based ecosystems, sustainable consumption and production)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>o All held together by the glue of 'peaceful and inclusive societies for sustainable development' (governance agenda, rule of law, violence).</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>17</mn><mtext>th&nbsp;</mtext></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">17^{\text {th }}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8491em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">7</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8491em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">th&nbsp;</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> goal covers means of implementation (finance, trade, technology, capacity building, partnerships, and data)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-sdgs-versus-mdgs">The SDGs versus MDGs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-sdgs-versus-mdgs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Key Strengths of the proposed SDGs include: -</li>
<li></li>
</ul>
<p>0 The notion of leaving no one behind - with many targets aspiring zero/fully coverage (raising the ambition of the MDGs)
0
0 Stand-alone goal of Inequality (within and between countries)
0
0 Stand-alone goal on gender inequality, including ending of all forms of violence, discrimination, child marriages, and female genital mutilations</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-sdgs-versus-mdgs">The SDGs versus MDGs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-sdgs-versus-mdgs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Environmental issues are strongly represented - fulfilling a long-sought marriage between development and environment (climate change, marine and land base ecosystems, and sustainable consumption and production)</li>
<li>Governance - for the first time - incorporating a goal and targets on governance and peaceful societies (legal identity, tackling corruption and bribery etc)</li>
<li>Participatory/Inclusiveness Process in formulation of the SDGs: The participation and buy in of a wide range of stakeholders including member states and non-governmental organizations</li>
<li>The broad nature of the SDG is also a reflection of the nature of challenges facing the world today</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="kenya-sdg-targets-for-rh">Kenya SDG Targets For RH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kenya-sdg-targets-for-rh" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Kenya RMNCAH Investment Framework (January 2016)</li>
<li>The Kenya RMNCAH investment framework sets ambitious targets to increase:</li>
<li>o skilled deliveries to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>87</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">87 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">87%</span></span></span></span></span>,</li>
<li>o 4+ ANC visits to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>69</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">69 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">69%</span></span></span></span></span>,</li>
<li>o full immunization to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>76</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">76 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">76%</span></span></span></span></span>,</li>
<li>o contraceptive use by currently married women in reproductive age to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>73</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">73 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">73%</span></span></span></span></span>, and</li>
<li>o pregnant women tested for HIV who received results and post-test counseling to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>75</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">75 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">75%</span></span></span></span></span> by 2020 from the</li>
</ul>
<table><thead><tr><th></th><th>baselines of the Kenya Demographic and Health Survey 2014 with enhanced focus on quality of services.</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>-</td><td>It also aims to reduce stunting to 19%, teenage pregnancy to 11%, and contribute to decrease in neonatal mortality to 18%.</td></tr><tr><td>-</td><td>The absolute number of deaths of children under-five years is projected to reduce from 77,761 to 48,590 and maternal from 5,453 to 3,276 between 2014/15 and 2019/20.</td></tr><tr><td>-</td><td>Finally, the framework aims to ensure that at least three out of four births will be registered, thereby providing more robust denominators to effectively plan and monitor RMNCAH service delivery.</td></tr><tr><td>-</td><td>Progress on improvements in quality, productivity and efficiency will be tracked through strengthened routine data, independent surveys, and implementation research of innovations.</td></tr><tr><td>-</td><td>Impact and outcome level indicators in reducing neonatal, infant, and under-five mortality rates, and maternal mortality ratio (MMR) will be tracked through population-based surveys such as the KDHS.</td></tr><tr><td>-</td><td>The proposed Maternal Death Surveillance and Response (MDSR) helps to identify and register maternal deaths, and support appropriate actions to be implemented to prevent them.</td></tr><tr><td>-</td><td>Active citizensâ€™ participation and feedback, independent verification and progress reviews will be used to track achievements of the investments made in RMNCAH.</td></tr><tr><td>-</td><td>Strengthening Civil Registration and Vital Statistics (CRVS) will be an essential intervention to inform better planning and enhance accountability to results.</td></tr></tbody></table>
