</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="superficial-fascia">Superficial fascia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#superficial-fascia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>This is continuous with the fatty and membranous layers of the anterior abdominal wall.</li>
<li>The fat is replaced by smooth muscle called the dartos muscle.</li>
<li>This is innervated by sympathetic nerve fibers and is responsible for the wrinkling of the overlying skin.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="spermatic-fasciae">Spermatic fasciae<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#spermatic-fasciae" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It has three layers which lie beneath the superficial fascia and are derived from the three layers of the anterior abdominal wall on each side.</li>
<li>The external spermatic fascia is derived from the aponeurosis of the external oblique muscle; the cremasteric fascia is derived from the internal oblique muscle; and, finally, the internal spermatic fascia is derived from the fascia transversalis.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tunica-vaginalis">Tunica vaginalis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tunica-vaginalis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>This lies within the spermatic fasciae and covers the anterior, medial, and lateral surfaces of each testis.</li>
</ul>
<p>Lymph from the skin and fascia, including the tunica vaginalis, drains into the superficial inguinal lymph nodes</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="testes">Testes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#testes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Testis has ellipsoid- shaped.</li>
<li>Testes develop in the abdomen and move before birth into the scrotum.</li>
<li>The left testis usually lies at a lower level than the right.</li>
<li>The testis are covered by:</li>
<li>A closed sac of peritoneum (the tunica vaginalis), which originally connected to the abdominal cavity. Normally after testicular descent, the connection closes, leaving a fibrous remnant.</li>
<li>It is covered by a fibrous capsule called the tunica albuginea.</li>
<li>In the inner surface of the capsule is a series of fibrous septa that divide the interior of the organ into lobules.</li>
<li>Lying within each lobule are 1 to 3 coiled seminiferous tubules.</li>
<li>The tubules open into a network of channels called the rete testis.</li>
<li>Small efferent ductules connect the rete testis to the upper end of the epididymis.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="epididymis">Epididymis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#epididymis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The epididymis is a single, long coiled duct that courses along the posterolateral side of the testis.</li>
<li>The tunica vaginalis covers the epididymis with the exception of the posterior border.</li>
<li>Structurally, epididymis divided into:</li>
</ul>
<p>0 Head
o Body
o tail</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="epididymis">Epididymis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#epididymis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It has two distinct components:</p>
<ul>
<li>The efferent ductules, which form an enlarged coiled mass that sits on the posterior superior pole of the testis and forms the head of the epididymis;</li>
<li>The true epididymis, which is a single, long coiled duct into which the efferent ductules all drain, and which continues inferiorly along the posterolateral margin of the testis as the body of epididymis and enlarges to form the tail of epididymis at the inferior pole of the testis.</li>
<li>The testicular artery is a branch of the abdominal aorta.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="venous-drainage-of-the-testis-and-epididymis">Venous drainage of the Testis and Epididymis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#venous-drainage-of-the-testis-and-epididymis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The testicular veins emerge from the testis and the epididymis as a venous network, the pampiniform plexus.</li>
<li>This becomes reduced to a single vein as it ascends through the inguinal canal.</li>
<li>The right testicular vein drains into the inferior vena cava, and the left vein joins the left renal vein.</li>
<li>Lymphatic drainage of the testes is to the para- aortic lymph nodes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ductus-deferens">Ductus deferens<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ductus-deferens" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>(Latin: "carrying-away vessel"), also called vas deferens.</li>
<li>The ductus deferens is a long muscular duct that transports spermatozoa from the tail of the epididymis to the ejaculatory duct</li>
<li>The vas arises from the tail of the epididymis and traverses the inguinal canal to the deep ring, passes downwards on the lateral wall of the pelvis almost to the ischial tuberosity and turns medially to cross the ureter posterior to the bladder.</li>
<li>It continues inferomedially along the base of the bladder, anterior to the rectum, almost to the midline, where it is joined by the duct of the seminal vesicle to form the ejaculatory duct.</li>
<li>The terminal part of the vas deferens is dilated to form the ampulla of the vas deferens.</li>
<li>The ejaculatory duct penetrates through the prostate gland to connect with the prostatic urethra.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="seminal-vesicle">Seminal vesicle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#seminal-vesicle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The seminal vesicles are an accessory gland of the male reproductive system.</li>
<li>The seminal vesicles are two lobulated organs about 2 in . ( 5 cm ) long lying on the posterior surface of the bladder</li>
<li>On the medial side of each vesicle lies the terminal part of the vas deferens.</li>
<li>Posteriorly, the seminal vesicles are related to the rectum.</li>
<li>Inferiorly, each seminal vesicle narrows and joins the vas deferens of the same side to form the ejaculatory duct.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="arteries">- Arteries<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#arteries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The arterial blood supply from, the inferior vesicle and middle rectal arteries</li>
<li>Veins</li>
<li>The veins drain into the internal iliac veins.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ejaculatory-ducts">Ejaculatory Ducts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ejaculatory-ducts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The two ejaculatory ducts are each less than 1 in. ( 2.5 cm ) long and are formed by the union of the vas deferens and the duct of the seminal vesicle.</li>
<li>The ejaculatory ducts pierce the posterior surface of the prostate and open into the prostatic part of the urethra, close to the margins of the prostatic utricle; their function is to drain the seminal fluid into the prostatic urethra.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prostate">Prostate<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prostate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The prostate is an unpaired accessory structure of the male reproductive system that surrounds the urethra in the pelvic cavity.</li>
<li>It lies immediately inferior to the bladder, above the urogenital diaphragm, posterior to the pubic symphysis, and anterior to the rectum.</li>
<li>The prostate is shaped like an inverted rounded cone with a larger base, which is continuous above with the neck of the bladder, and a narrower apex, which rests below on the pelvic floor.</li>
<li>The inferolateral surfaces of the prostate are in contact with the levator ani muscles that together cradle the prostate between them.</li>
<li>The two ejaculatory ducts pierce the upper part of the posterior surface of the prostate to open into the prostatic urethra at the lateral margins of the prostatic utricle.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="relations-of-prostate">Relations of Prostate<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#relations-of-prostate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Superiorly</li>
<li>The base of the prostate is continuous with the neck of the bladder.</li>
<li>The urethra enters the center of the base of the prostate.</li>
<li>Inferiorly</li>
<li>The apex of the prostate lies on the upper surface of the urogenital diaphragm.</li>
<li>The urethra leaves the prostate just above the apex on the anterior surface</li>
<li>Anteriorly</li>
<li>The prostate is related to the symphysis pubis.</li>
<li>The prostate is connected to the posterior aspect of the pubic bones by the puboprostatic ligaments.</li>
<li>Laterally</li>
</ul>
<p>o The prostate is embraced by the anterior fibers of the levator ani.</p>
<ul>
<li>Posteriorly
o The prostate is closely related to the anterior surface of the rectal ampulla and is separated from it by the rectovesical septum (fascia of Denonvilliers).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="structure-of-the-prostate">Structure of the Prostate<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#structure-of-the-prostate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Enclosed within thin dense fibrous capsule</li>
<li>Inner loose sheath derived from pelvic fascia - "prostatic sheath"</li>
<li>Continuous inferiorly with superior fascia of urogenital diaphragm</li>
<li>Posteriorly it is part of rectovesical septum</li>
<li>Separates bladder, seminal vesicles and prostate from rectum</li>
<li>Prostatic venous plexus lies between fibrous capsule and prostatic sheath.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prostate-divided-into">Prostate divided into:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prostate-divided-into" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Two lateral lobes</li>
<li>One median lobe</li>
<li>Anterior and posterior lobes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="structure-of-the-prostate">Structure of the Prostate<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#structure-of-the-prostate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Anterior</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tissue lying anterior to urethra</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>No glands; fibromuscular tissue only</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Median</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cone-shaped region between ejaculatory ducts and urethra</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lateral (left &amp; right)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Main mass of gland, continuous posteriorly</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Separated by prostatic urethra</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Posterior</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Describes postero-medial part of lateral lobes palpable through rectum on DRE.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="blood-supply-of-the-prostate">Blood Supply of The Prostate<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#blood-supply-of-the-prostate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Arterial supply</li>
<li>Arteries derived from internal pudenal, inferior vesical and middle rectal arteries (branches of internal iliac)</li>
<li>Venous drainage</li>
<li>Veins form prostatic venous plexus around sides and base of prostate - located between capsule and sheath</li>
<li>Drains into internal iliac veins</li>
<li>Also communicates with vesical venous plexus and vertebral venous plexuses.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lymphatics-and-innervation-of-the-prostate">Lymphatics and innervation of The Prostate<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lymphatics-and-innervation-of-the-prostate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>o Lymphatic drainage
Â§ Lymph vessels terminate in internal iliac and sacral lymph nodes
Â§ Some vessels from posterior surface pass with lymph vessels from bladder to external iliac LN's</p>
<ul>
<li>Innervation
Â§ Parasympathetic fibres arise from pelvic splanchnic nerves
Â§ Sympathetic fibres from inferior hypogastric plexuses</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="penis">Penis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#penis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The penis is a pendulous organ suspended from the front and sides of the pubic arch and containing the greater part of the urethra.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It consists of internal root, external shaft, &amp; glans.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Root: the portion of the penis that extends internally into the pelvic cavity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Shaft: the length of the penis between the glans and the body.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Glans: the head of the penis; has many nerve endings.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Foreskin: a covering of skin over the penile glans.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The root of penis consists of the two crura, which are proximal parts of the corpora cavernosa attached to the pubic arch, and the bulb of penis, which is the proximal part of the corpus spongiosum anchored to the perineal membrane.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The body of the penis is essentially composed of three cylinders of erectile tissue enclosed in a tubular sheath of fascia (Buck's fascia).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The erectile tissue is made up of two dorsally placed corpora cavernosa and a single corpus spongiosum applied to their ventral surface.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>At its distal extremity, the corpus spongiosum expands to form the glans penis, which covers the distal ends of the corpora cavernosa.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>On the tip of the glans penis is the slit like orifice of the urethra, called the external urethral meatus.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="external-penile-structures">External penile structures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#external-penile-structures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Corona: the rim of the penile glans.</li>
<li>Frenulum: thin strip of skin connecting the glans to the shaft on the underside of the penis.</li>
<li>Both are highly sensitive areas to the touch</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="blood-supply-of-the-penis">Blood Supply of The Penis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#blood-supply-of-the-penis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="arteries">Arteries<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#arteries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The corpora cavernosa is supplied by the deep arteries of the penis; the corpus spongiosum is supplied by the artery of the bulb.</li>
<li>In addition, there is the dorsal artery of the penis.</li>
<li>All the above arteries are branches of the internal pudendal artery.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="veins">Veins<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#veins" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The veins drain into the internal pudendal veins.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="lymphatics-and-innervation-of-the-penis">Lymphatics and innervation of The Penis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lymphatics-and-innervation-of-the-penis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lymph-drainage">Lymph Drainage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lymph-drainage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The skin of the penis is drained into the medial group of superficial inguinal nodes.</li>
<li>The deep structures of the penis are drained into the internal iliac nodes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nerve-supply">Nerve Supply<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nerve-supply" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Sensation</li>
<li>The nerve supply is from the pudendal nerve and the pelvic plexuses.</li>
<li>Erectile function</li>
<li>Parasympathetic(excitatory)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sympathetic-inhibitory">Sympathetic (inhibitory)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sympathetic-inhibitory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="summary">Summary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="penis-nerve-supply">Penis Nerve Supply<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#penis-nerve-supply" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Sensation</li>
<li>The nerve supply is from the pudendal nerve and the pelvic plexuses.</li>
<li>Erectile function</li>
<li>Parasympathetic (excitatory)</li>
<li>Sympathetic (inhibitory)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unit-three-content">Unit Three Content.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-three-content" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="topic-1-obstetrics-history-taking">Topic 1: Obstetrics History Taking<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#topic-1-obstetrics-history-taking" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="confidentiality">CONFIDENTIALITY:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#confidentiality" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>During history taking, the medical student should at all times show the patient the res pect that is due to her; while full confidentiality must be maintained at all times bearing in mind that the</p>
<p>relationship between the professional and his client is based on mutual trust and res pect.</p>
<p>Classical Hippocratic Oath state: "All that may come to my knowledge in the exer cise of my profession or in daily commerce with men, which ought not to be spread abroad, I will keep secret and will never reveal."</p>
<p>Criminal Code of Malta [Ch.9:257]. The law reads as follows: "If any physician, surge on, obstetrician or apothecary or, in general, any other person who, by reason of his calling or profession, becomes the
depository of any secret confided to him, shall, except when compelled by law to giv e information to the public authority, disclose such secret, he shall, on conviction be I iable to a fine."</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="history-taking-in-obstetrics">HISTORY TAKING IN OBSTETRICS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#history-taking-in-obstetrics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

Ã˜ "Hello. I am Mr/Ms *****, a medical student. Do you mind if I ask you some questio ns about your medical condition?"</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-particulars">2. PARTICULARS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-particulars" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ã˜ Name, age, address, marital status, occupation, religion, sex.
Ã˜ LMP, parity, gravity, EDD - Naegele's rule</p>
<p>o Gravidity is no. of pregnancies including current pregnancy (regardless of the outcome Normal or abortion)
o Parity is no. of births beyond 24 wk gestation</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-presenting-complaint">3. PRESENTING COMPLAINT:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-presenting-complaint" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âˆ…</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\varnothing</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6633em; vertical-align: -0.0817em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âˆ…</span></span></span></span></span> "What is the problem that brought you to the hospital/clinic?"
Ã˜ I Best to record this in the patient's own words.
Ã˜ J "Were you referred by your doctor or did you self-refer yourself to the hospital/clinic?"
Ã˜ Duration of the presenting complain.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-history-of-present-illness-hpi">4. HISTORY OF PRESENT ILLNESS (HPI)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-history-of-present-illness-hpi" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ã˜ In the obstetric patient, its may be best to consider the "presenting complaint" in <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>t</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">t</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6151em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">t</span></span></span></span></span> wo
parts:
a. The history of present illness or complaint; and
b. The history of the current pregnancy.</p>
<p>Patient may not furnish sufficient details, in which case it will be necessary to amplify with specific</p>
<p>Directed questions. E.g. SOCRATES relating to pain: -
i. Site: where, local/diffuse
ii. Onset: rapid/gradual, pattern, worse/better since onset
iii. Character: sharp/dull/stabbing, burning/cramp/crushing
iv. Radiation: "Does the pain affect you anywhere else?" [to thigh/loin/ elsewhere]
v. Alleviating factors: "What do you do to make yourself comfortable?" "Is the pain better after menstruation?"</p>
<p>vi. Time course: "When did the pain start?"; if pain is chronic "What made you seek attention now" "Is the pain worse at any particular time of the cycle?"
vii. Exacerbating factors: "Is there anything that brings on the pain or makes it worse?"
viii. Severity &amp; Impact on life: "On a scale of 1 to 10, at what level would you classif y the pain?"
"Does it interrupt your life?"</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-obstetric-history">6. <div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-history-of-present-pregnancy">A. HISTORY OF PRESENT PREGNANCY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-history-of-present-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-menstrual-history">a. Menstrual history<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-menstrual-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ã¼ The date of the first day of the last menstrual period (or LMP).
Ã¼ The length of the menstrual cycle refers to the time interval between the first day of the period and</p>
<p>the first day of the subsequent period. This may vary from 21 to 35 days in normal w omen, but menstruation usually occurs every 28 days</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="b-the-estimated-date-of-delivery-edd">b. The estimated date of delivery (EDD)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-the-estimated-date-of-delivery-edd" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Ã¼ Can be calculated from the first day of the last menstrual period (LMP) by adding 9 months and 7 days to this date.
Ã¼ However, to apply this Naegele's rule, LMP should be accurate and the woman should have had regular 28day menstrual cycles.
Ã¼ The average duration of human gestation is 269 days from the date of conception
Ã¼ Therefore, in a woman with a 28day cycle, this is 283 days from the first day of the last menstrual
period (14 days are added for the period between menstruation and conception)
Ã¼ In a 28
day cycle, the estimated date of delivery can be calculated by subtracting 3 months <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>f</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">f</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.10764em;">f</span></span></span></span></span> rom the first day
of the LMP and adding on 7 days (or alternatively, adding 9 months and 7 days).
Ã¼ It is important to
appreciate that only <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>40</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">40 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">40%</span></span></span></span></span> of women will deliver within 5days of the EDD and about twothirds of women deliver within 10 days of EDD.
Ã¼ The calculation of EDD based on a woman's LMP is therefore, at best, a guide to a woman as to the
date around which her delivery is likely to occur.
Ã¼ If a woman's normal menstrual cycle is less than 28 days or is greater than 28 day s, then an
appropriate number of days should be subtracted from or added to the estimated dat e of delivery.
Ã¼ For example, if the normal cycle is 35 days, 7 days should be added to the estimat ed date of delivery</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-gravity">a. GRAVITY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-gravity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ã¼The term 'gravidity' refers to the number of times a woman has been pregnant, irre spective of the
outcome of the pregnancy, i.e. termination, miscarriage or ectopic pregnancy.
Ã¼ A primigravida is a woman who is pregnant for the first time and a multigravida is a woman who has been pregnant on two or more occasions.</p>
<p>Ã¼ This term 'gravidity' must be distinguished from the term 'parity', which describes th e number of liveborn children and stillbirths a woman has delivered after 24 weeks or with a birth weight of 500 g .
Ã¼ Thus, a primipara is a woman who has given birth to one infant after 24 weeks.
Ã¼ A multiparous woman is one who has given birth to two or more infants, whereas, a nulliparous woman has not given birth after 24 weeks.
Ã¼ The term 'grand multipara' has been used to describe a woman who has given birth to five or more infants
Ã¼ A parturient is a woman in labour and a puerpera is a woman who has given birth <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>t</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">t</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6151em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">t</span></span></span></span></span> o a child during the preceding 42 days.
b. Gestation by dates
c. FOCUSED ANTENATAL CLINIC
Ã¼When started, number of visits so far
Ã¼antenatal profile
o haemoglobin
o blood groups &amp; rhesus factor
o syphilis test - VDRL / RPR
o HIV test
o Urinalysis
o Optional : blood slide for MPS, Stool for ova &amp; cyst
Ã¼Medication presently and previously
Ã¼Radiological examinations during pregnancy
d. Assess about Symptoms of pregnancy and their severity
Ã¼ Nausea and vomiting</p>
<p>o commonly occur within 2 weeks of missing the first period and it is believed to be secondary to human chorionic gonadotrophin (hCG.
o it is described as morning sickness, vomiting may occur at any time of the day and is often precipitated by the smell or sight of food.
o Morning sickness commonly occurs in the first 3 months but, in some women, it may persist throughout pregnancy
o Severe and persistent vomiting leading to maternal dehydration, ketonuria and electrolyte imbalance is termed hyperemesis gravidarum
Ã¼ Increased frequency of micturition
o due to the pressure on the bladder exerted by the gravid uterus.
o It tends to diminish after the first 12 weeks of pregnancy as the uterus rises above the symphysis pubis, i.e. into the larger abdominal cavity.
Ã¼ Excessive lassitude or lethargy
o is a common symptom of early pregnancy and may become apparent even before the first period is missed.
o Often, it disappears after 12 weeks of gestation.
Ã¼ Breast tenderness and heaviness,
o which are really an extension of those experienced by many
women in the premenstrual
phase of the cycle, are common during early pregnancy.
o It is due to the effect of increasing serum progesterone as well as an increased retention of water.
Ã¼ First maternal perception of fetal movements, also called 'quickening'
o is not usually noticed until 20 weeks gestation during first pregnancy and 18 weeks in the second or subsequent pregnancies.
o However, many women may experience fetal movements earlier than 18 weeks a nd others may progress beyond 20 weeks of gestation without being aware of fetal movements at all.
Ã¼ Some women may experience an abnormal desire for a particular food and this is termed pica
Ã¼ Pseudocyesis</p>
<p>o Development of symptoms and many of the signs of pregnancy in a woman who is not pregnant.
o This is often due to an intense desire for or fears of pregnancy that may result in hypothalamic amenorrhoea
Ã¼ Leg cramps
Ã¼ Limb swelling
e. Enquire about symptoms which could indicate complications of pregnancy
Ã¼Per vaginal discharge, bleeding
Ã¼LAPs
Ã¼Headache
Ã¼Visual disturbance
Ã¼Pain on micturation</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="f-previous-obstetric-history-previous-deliveries-miscarriages">f. PREVIOUS OBSTETRIC HISTORY(Previous deliveries/miscarriages)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#f-previous-obstetric-history-previous-deliveries-miscarriages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Ã¼Detail each previous pregnancy - dates of deliveries, where birth took place, delivered at what gestation, how long did labour take, mode of delivery, condition of baby at birth, sex, birth weight, other complications at delivery and postpartum, any blood transufusion, did she breast fed if not why, Length of labour &amp; complications, outcome, Previous miscarriages</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="general-examination-techniques">General Examination Techniques<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-examination-techniques" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prerequisites-when-examining-a-patient">Prerequisites when examining a patient<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prerequisites-when-examining-a-patient" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Use your senses well - listen, look, touch, smell, when examining</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Knowledge of anatomical land marks</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensure adequate lighting in the room &amp; Secondary tangential lighting from a lamp</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensure the place is quiet to allow proper percussion and auscultation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensure presence of necessary instruments</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ensure privacy.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Explain the procedure to the patient and ask permission to examine</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Be thorough without wasting time, systemic without being rigid, gentle yet not afraid to cause discomfort</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Try to look calm, organized and competent even if you do not exactly feel that way</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Avoid expressions of disgust, alarm, distaste, or other negative reaction</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sequence the comprehensive examination in a manner designed to minimize the patient's need to change positions and maximize your efficiency. Variations are possible and you may wish to develop a method of your own. In general it is helpful to move from head to toe.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Examine patient from the right side. Working from one side helps you master skills more quickly and promotes efficiency. Left-handed students find it awkward but are encouraged to practice it for convenience of themselves and others</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="general-techniques-used-in-physical-examination">GENERAL TECHNIQUES USED IN PHYSICAL EXAMINATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-techniques-used-in-physical-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-inspection">1. Inspection:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-inspection" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Definition: it's the process of observing signs indicative of a healthy or a pathological state of a certain body part or system within a patient</li>
<li>Inspection should start as the patient enter consultation room (posture, gait, appropriate clothing, colour and moisture of skin, unusual odours), during history taking and during physical examination where you expose the areas of inspection as you validate the inspection findings with your patient ("I see a black spot here, have you noted it?)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-palpation">2. Palpation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-palpation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Definition: it involves the use of your hands and fingers to gather information through sense of touch.</li>
<li>Certain parts of the hands are better than others for specific types of palpation eg:
o Palmar surface &amp; finger pads are most suitable to assess position, texture, size, form, consistency and presence of fluid or crepitus of a mass or structure
o Ulnar surface of hands is suitable to assess vibration
o Dorsal surface of hands is suitable to assess temperature.</li>
<li>Palpation may be light or deep controlled by amount of pressure applied. Light palpation always precedes deep palpation.</li>
<li>On the abdomen: always begin the palpation process with light systemic palpation of four quadrants initially avoiding areas of tenderness or problem spot</li>
<li>Light palpation is important in eliciting areas of muscle resistance and tenderness.</li>
<li>Deep palpation is normally only done in the abdomen</li>
<li>Palpation can be made with one hand or by two hands on top of each other with the upper one exerting the pressure (reinforced palpation)</li>
</ul>
<p>Bimanual palpation is a technique whereby an organ is palpated using both hands.</p>
<p>Preparation: o Short nails o Patient to lie supine to relax abdominal muscles o Warm your hands to avoid producing muscle contractions o Stand on right of the patient (if the patient is in a low bed - sit on or kneel besides the patient's right) o Ensure patient is comfortable o Ask patient to show areas of pain before you start palpation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-percussion">3. Percussion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-percussion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Definition: it involves striking one object against another, thus providing vibration and subsequent sound waves.</p>
<ul>
<li>Your middle finger functions as the hammer and the vibration is produced by the impact of the finger against the underlying tissue.</li>
<li>Sound waves are heard as percussion tones (notes) that arise from vibrations in the body tissue</li>
<li>The degree of percussion tone is determined by the intensity of medium through which the sound waves travel eg air, fluid or solid:</li>
</ul>
<p>Example</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Tone</th><th>Intensity</th><th>Pitch</th><th>Duration</th><th>Quality</th><th>Example</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Tympanic</td><td>Loud</td><td>High</td><td>Moderate</td><td>Drum like</td><td>Gastric bubble</td></tr><tr><td>Hyper-</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>resonant</td><td>Very loud</td><td>Low</td><td>Long</td><td>Boom like</td><td>Emphysematous</td></tr><tr><td>lung</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Resonant</td><td>Loud</td><td>Low</td><td>Long</td><td>Hollow</td><td>Health lung</td></tr><tr><td>Dull</td><td>Soft to</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>moderate</td><td>Moderate to</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>high</td><td>Moderate</td><td>Thud like</td><td>Over liver</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Flat</td><td>Soft</td><td>High</td><td>Short</td><td>Very dull</td><td>Over muscle</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Percusion Technique</p>
<p>I. Your (dormant) middle finger acts as a hammer (plexor) and fingers on the other hand (non-dorminant) acts as the striking surface (pleximeter) spread over surface of the body. The middle finger should be slightly flexed, relaxed and posed to strike. Plexor should be at right angles with pleximeter. Snap the wrist of the tapping hand downwards, and with the tip of the plexor sharply tap the interphalangeal joint or second phalanx of pleximeter</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nb-the-downward-snap-of-the-striking-finger-originates-from-the-wrist-and-not-from-movement-in-the-forearm-or-shoulder-it-should-be-quick-sharp-but-relaxed-wrist-motion">NB. The downward snap of the striking finger originates from the wrist and not from movement in the forearm or shoulder. It should be quick, sharp but relaxed wrist motion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nb-the-downward-snap-of-the-striking-finger-originates-from-the-wrist-and-not-from-movement-in-the-forearm-or-shoulder-it-should-be-quick-sharp-but-relaxed-wrist-motion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Once your finger has struck, snap the wrist back quickly lifting the finger to prevent dampening the sound.</p>
<p>Use the tip and not the pad of the flexor finger
You can percuss one location several times for ease interpretation of the tone
II. Alternative technique:
Ã¼ Strike your finger or hand directly against the body eg clavicle and skull
(hydrocephalus)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-auscultation">4. AUSCULTATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-auscultation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Definition: means listening for sounds produced by the body.</li>
<li>It should be carried out last after the other techniques have provided information that will assist in interpreting what you hear</li>
<li>NB. Only abdomen you auscultate before palpation and percussion as the latter two techniques sometimes influence the bowel sounds.</li>
<li>Technique:
o Ensure a quiet environment</li>
<li>Place bell or diaphragm of the stethoscope on naked skin as clothing obscures sound</li>
<li>Stabilize the stethoscope by holding the chest piece between the second and third finger.</li>
<li>When using the diaphragm press it firmly against the skin.</li>
<li>Avoid touching the tubing with your hands or allowing it rub against any surface as it creates extraneous noise.</li>
</ul>
<p>o Listen to sound not only for its presence or absence but also for its characteristics - intensity, pitch, duration and quality
o Closing your eyes may help you focus on the sound
o Target and isolate each sound, concentrating on one sound at a time.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="general-examination-and-vital-signs">General Examination and Vital Signs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-examination-and-vital-signs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general-examination">General examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Observe the patients general state of health, height, built and sexual development</li>
<li>Note posture, motor activity, gait, dresss, grooming and personal hygiene any odours of the body and breath</li>
<li>Watch patient's facial expressions and notes manner and affect and reactions to things in the environment</li>
<li>Listen to manner of speaking and note state of awareness</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-parameters">CLINICAL PARAMETERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-parameters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-pallor">1. PALLOR:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-pallor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ã¼ Sites in the body to examine pallor
v Conjunctiva
v Tongue
v Palms
v Nail bed: capillary refill
v Sole of foot
v Anus/ perineum</p>
<p>Conjunctiva: ask patient to be seated or lie supine, facing you. Place both thumbs on the margins of the lower eyelids and gently pull the skin downwards to evert lower lids (palpebral conjunctiva) and examine colour.</p>
<p>Tongue /lips: ask patient to open mouth and protrude the tongue. Observe colour of the tongue. Pull and evert the upper and lower lips gently to observe colour of inner parts.</p>
<p>Palms: ask the patient to supinate the two palms. Observe colour while you compare with your own palms</p>
<p>Capillary refill test: blanch the nail bed with the thumb and sustain the pressure for several seconds on fingernail or toenail. Release the pressure, observe the time elapsed before the nail regains its full colour. Normally this should occur almost instantly - in less than 2seconds.</p>
<p>Soles: with the patient lying supine or seated: look at the soles and observe colour</p>
<p>Anus / perineum: patient in lithotomy position (supine, hips and knees flexed) or lying on side, assess the perineum / anus for colour if applicable. Use gloves</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-jaundice">2. JAUNDICE:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-jaundice" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âˆ…</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\varnothing</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6633em; vertical-align: -0.0817em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âˆ…</span></span></span></span></span> Means having a yellowish discoloration.
Ã˜ Can be observed at: sclera, mucous membranes and skin
Ã˜ With patient seated or supine, gently elevate upper eyelids using both thumbs with patient facing a light source, ask him/her to look downwards to expose sclera and assess colour.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">âˆ…</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\varnothing</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6633em; vertical-align: -0.0817em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">âˆ…</span></span></span></span></span> Ask patient to open mouth assess colour of mucous membrane
Ã˜ Examine skin and assess colour - light skinned people and infants.
Ã˜ Look at palms and soles for yellowish discoloration</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-hypoxaemia-cyanosis">3. HYPOXAEMIA : CYANOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-hypoxaemia-cyanosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A bluish discolouration these sites
TYPES:</p>
<ul>
<li>Central cyanosis - lips &amp; frenulum and</li>
<li>peripheral cyanosis - extremities at hands and feets
examine palms, sole, lips and frenulum for colour</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="4-hypoxaemia-finger-clubbing">4. HYPOXAEMIA: FINGER CLUBBING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-hypoxaemia-finger-clubbing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>I. look at the shape of nails as compare with yours
a. Nail base angle should measure about 160 degrees.
b. Observe this by placing a ruler or a sheet paper across the nail and dorsal surface of the finger and examine the angle formed by the proximal nail fold and nail plate.
II. In clubbing the angle increases and approaches or exceeds 180 degrees
a. Ask the patient to place together the nail (dorsal) surfaces of the fingertips from the right and left hands
b. When nails are clubbed, the diamond - shaped window at the base of the nails disappears and the angle between the distal tips increases (shamroth technique)
III. Gently squeeze nail between your thumb and the pad of your finger to test for adherence of the nail to the nail bed.
a. The nail bed should feel firm
b. A boggy nail base accompanies clubbing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-dehydration">5. DEHYDRATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-dehydration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sites: fontanels, eyes, mucous membranes, skin (abdomen or chest)
Fontanels - below 18months - sunken in dehydration
Eyes - sunken in dehydration. Absent tears in dehydration
Mucous membranes - dry in dehydration
Skin turgor - pinch skin over chest or abdomen using thumb and index finger. Observe duration skin takes to go back.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-oedema">6. OEDEMA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-oedema" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Sites: face, sacrum, abdomen. Extremities.
Face: observe peri-orbital oedema
Sacrum: press sacral area with thumb for 30seconds</p>
<p>Lower limbs: use both thumbs to apply pressure on the lower limbs 1 cm above medial malleolus for 30seconds as you look patient face.assess for pitting by running you finger over the site</p>
<p>Report oedema as - bi- or unilateral, tender or non-tender, pitting or nonpitting.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7-lymph-nodes">7. LYMPH NODES.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-lymph-nodes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Ã¼ Small, mobile and painless lymph nodes are often palpable in healthy individuals
Ã¼ A painful lymph node is suggestive for inflammatory process
Ã¼ A firm or fixed non-motile LN is very suggestive for a malignant process
Technique:
Inspect area of LN for apparent LN, oedema, erythema, red streaks and skin lesions Using pads of <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>2</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">r</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi></mrow><msup><mn>3</mn><mtext>rd&nbsp;</mtext></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">&amp;</mi><msup><mn>4</mn><mtext>th&nbsp;</mtext></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">2 \mathrm{rd} 3^{\text {rd }} \&amp; 4^{\text {th }}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8491em;"></span><span class="mord">2</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">rd</span></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">3</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8491em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">rd&nbsp;</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord">&amp;</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">4</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8491em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">th&nbsp;</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> fingers gently palpatefor superficial nodes</p>
<p>Note location, consistency, mobility, tenderness, size, shape, discreteness &amp; warmth. Move skin over area.</p>
<p>Head &amp; neck LN: Palpate the anterior LN from behind the patient and vice varsa. Sternocleidomastoid muscle divide into anterior &amp; posterior</p>
<p>Axillary LN:
Other LN.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="8-oral-thrush">8. ORAL THRUSH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#8-oral-thrush" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vital-signs">VITAL SIGNS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vital-signs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The word vital signs means essential to life.
They include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Pulse rate</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Respiratory rate</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Blood pressure</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Temperature</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-pulse-rate">1. PULSE RATE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-pulse-rate" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Radial pulse is mostly used to assess:</p>
<ul>
<li>Heart rate</li>
<li>Cardiac cycles per minute</li>
<li>Collapsing pulse</li>
<li>Arrhythmias</li>
<li>Condition of the blood vessels</li>
<li>Assessing the blood pressure</li>
</ul>
<p>Sites for taking pulse rate:</p>
<ul>
<li>Radial: on the thumb side of the wrist</li>
<li>Temporal: lateral to eye brow on the temporal bone</li>
<li>Brachial: medial aspect of cubital fossa</li>
<li>Femoral: upper inner aspect of thigh</li>
<li>Popliteal: behind the knee</li>
<li>Dorsalis pedis: upper surface of the foot</li>
<li>Carotid pulse: side of the neck</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-of-pulse">Characteristics of pulse<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-pulse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ã¼ Rhythm:
o Regular
o Irregular
Â§ Regular irregular
Â§ Irregular irregular
Ã¼ Character:
o Feeble (small volume - eg dehydration)</p>
<p>o Pounding eg anxiety
o Collapsing
Ã¼ Pulse volume.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-blood-pressure">2. BLOOD PRESSURE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-blood-pressure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
