<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="unit-four-content">Unit Four Content..<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-four-content" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="topic-1-puberty">Topic 1: PUBERTY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#topic-1-puberty" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Period when the endocrine and gametogenic functions of the gonads have first developed to the point where reproduction is possible</p>
<p>This is characterized by sequence of events by which a child becomes a young adult:</p>
<p>The beginning of gametogenesis
Secretion of gonadal hormones
Development of secondary sexual characters and reproductive functions
Sexual dimorphism is accentuated.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="factors-affecting-the-onset-of-puberty">Factors affecting the onset of puberty<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-affecting-the-onset-of-puberty" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The age of onset of puberty varies and is more closely correlated with osseous maturation than with chronological age</p>
<p>Genetic/Ethnic factors
Environmental/Geographical factors</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prepubertal-stage-8-9-yr-of-age">Prepubertal stage (8-9 yr of age)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prepubertal-stage-8-9-yr-of-age" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The hypothalamic-anterior pituitary-gonadal axis is suppressed by;
Neuronal restraint pathways
Negative feedback provided by minute amounts of circulating gonadal steroids
Thus there are undetectable serum levels of;
luteinizing hormone (LH)
sex hormones (i.e., estradiol in girls, testosterone in boys)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prepuberty-stage">PREPUBERTY STAGE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prepuberty-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Evidence of hypothalamic-anterior pituitary-gonadal interaction during the prepubertal period resides in the fact that serum follicle-stimulating hormone (FSH) concentrations are detectable in most children and may be increased (with serum LH concentrations) in;</p>
<p>Turner syndrome
Anorchia</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="peripubertal-period-1-3-yr-before-the-onset-of-puberty">Peripubertal period (1-3 yr before the onset of puberty)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#peripubertal-period-1-3-yr-before-the-onset-of-puberty" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pulsatile secretion of low levels of LH during sleep secondary to endogenous episodic discharge of hypothalamic gonadotropin-releasing hormone (GnRH).</p>
<p>Nocturnal pulses of LH continue to increase in amplitude and, to a lesser extent, in frequency as clinical puberty approaches.</p>
<p>Serum LH concentrations rise earlier in the course of the pubertal process in boys than in girls.</p>
<p>This pulsatile secretion of gonadotropins is responsible for;
Enlargement and maturation of the gonads
The secretion of sex hormones
Appearance of the secondary sex characteristics</p>
<p>NB</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="gnrh-is-the-major-if-not-the-only-hormone-responsible-for-the-onset-and-progression-of-puberty">GnRH is the major, if not the only, hormone responsible for the onset and progression of puberty.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gnrh-is-the-major-if-not-the-only-hormone-responsible-for-the-onset-and-progression-of-puberty" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A second critical event occurs in middle or late adolescence in girls, in whom cyclicity and ovulation occur.</p>
<p>A positive-feedback mechanism develops whereby rising levels of estrogen in midcycle cause a distinct increase of LH.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="puberty-in-girls-8-13yr">Puberty in Girls (8-13yr)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#puberty-in-girls-8-13yr" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Thelarche (Development of Breasts) - Breast bud - 10-11 yrs
Pubarche (Development of axillary and pubic hair) - Appearance of pubic hair - 6-12 mo later</p>
<p>Peak height velocity occurs early (at breast stage II-III, typically between 11 and 12 yr of age) in girls and always precedes menarche.</p>
<p>Menarche (first menstrual period) Interval to menarche - 2-2.5 yr but may be as long as 6 yr after thelarche.</p>
<p>Mean age of menarche - 12.75 yr. (13.5 yrs in rural girls)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="puberty-in-boys-9-14yr">Puberty in Boys (9-14yr)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#puberty-in-boys-9-14yr" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Growth of the testes ( <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>&gt;</mo><mn>3</mn><mrow><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">L</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">&gt;3 \mathrm{~mL}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">&gt;</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">3</span><span class="mord"><span class="mspace nobreak">&nbsp;</span><span class="mord mathrm">mL</span></span></span></span></span></span> in volume or 2.5 cm in longest diameter)
Thinning of the scrotum
Pigmentation of the scrotum
Growth of the penis, seminal vesicles and prostrate</p>
<p>Pubic hair then appears
Appearance of axillary hair usually occurs in midpuberty, 2 yr after pubic hair.
In boys, unlike girls, acceleration of growth (5-15cm/yr in early adolescence but later drops) begins after puberty is well under way and is maximal at genital stage IV-V (typically between 13 and 14 yr of age).</p>
<p>In boys, the growth spurt occurs approximately 2 yr later than in girls, and growth may continue beyond 18 yr of age.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="adrenarche">Adrenarche<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adrenarche" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Adrenal cortical androgens also play a role in pubertal maturation.
Serum levels of dehydroepiandrosterone (DHEA) and its sulfate (DHEAS) begin to rise at approximately <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>6</mn><mo>âˆ’</mo><mn>8</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">6-8</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">6</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">âˆ’</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">8</span></span></span></span></span> yr of age, before any increase in LH or sex hormones and before the earliest physical changes of puberty are apparent.</p>
<p>NB
DHEAS is the most abundant adrenal C-19 steroid in the blood, and its serum concentration remains fairly stable over 24 hr ; a single measurement of this hormone is commonly used as a marker of adrenal androgen secretion.</p>
<p>Although adrenarche typically antedates the onset of gonadal activity (i.e., gonadarche) by a few years, the two processes do not seem to be causally related, because adrenarche and gonadarche are dissociated in conditions such as;</p>
<p>Central precocious puberty
Adrenocortical failure</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="endocrinology-in-puberty">ENDOCRINOLOGY IN PUBERTY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#endocrinology-in-puberty" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The levels of gonadal steroids and gonadotropins are low until the age of 6-8 yrs
This is mainly due to the negative feedback effect of estrogen to the hypothalamic pituitary system (Gonadostat).</p>
<p>The gonadostat remains very sensitive (6-15 times) to the negative feedback effect, even though the level of estradiol is very low ( <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>10</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">p</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">l</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">10 \mathrm{pg} / \mathrm{ml}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">10</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">pg</span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">ml</span></span></span></span></span></span> ) during that time.</p>
<p>As puberty approaches this negative feedback effect of estrogen is gradually lost.
This results in some significant changes in the endocrine function of the girl.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hypothalamopituitary-gonadal-axis">Hypothalamopituitary gonadal axis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hypothalamopituitary-gonadal-axis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The GnRH pulses from hypothalamus results in pulsatile gonadotropin secretion (first during the night then by the day time).</p>
<p>GnRH <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>â†’</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\rightarrow</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.3669em;"></span><span class="mrel">â†’</span></span></span></span></span> FSH, LH <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>â†’</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\rightarrow</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.3669em;"></span><span class="mrel">â†’</span></span></span></span></span> Estradiol
The tonic and episodic secretion of gonadotropins in prepubertal period is gradually changed to one of cyclic release in postpubertal period</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adrenal-glands-adrenarche">Adrenal glands (Adrenarche)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adrenal-glands-adrenarche" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>increase their activity of sex steroid synthesis (androstenedione, DHA, DHAS) from about 7 years of age.</p>
<p>Increased sebum formation, pubic and axillary hair and change in voice are primarily due to adrenal androgen production.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gonadarche">Gonadarche:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gonadarche" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Increased amplitude and frequency of GnRH <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>â†’</mo><mo>â†‘</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\rightarrow \uparrow</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mrel">â†’â†‘</span></span></span></span></span> secretion of FSH and LH <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>â†’</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\rightarrow</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.3669em;"></span><span class="mrel">â†’</span></span></span></span></span> ovarian follicular development <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>â†’</mo><mo>â†‘</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\rightarrow \uparrow</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mrel">â†’â†‘</span></span></span></span></span> estrogen.</p>
<p>Gonadal estrogen is responsible for the development of uterus, vagina, vulva and also the breasts</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="menarche">Menarche<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#menarche" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The onset of first menstruation in life is called menarche.
It may occur anywhere between 10 and 16 years, the peak time being 13 years.
The first period is usually anovular.
The ovulation may be irregular for a variable period following menarche and may take about 2 years for regular ovulation to occur.</p>
<p>The menses may be irregular to start with.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adolescence">ADOLESCENCE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adolescence" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The period of life beginning with puberty and ending with completed growth and physical maturity.</p>
<p>Between the ages of 10 - 19 yr (WHO), children undergo rapid changes in;</p>
<p>Phenotypic changes: - Body size &amp; Body shape
Neuroendocrine changes - Hormones set the developmental agenda in conjunction with social structures designed to foster the transition from childhood to adulthood.</p>
<p>Physiology
Psychological functioning
Social functioning
NB: 10-24 yr - Young Adults
Marshall - Tanner Classification of Sex Maturity Stages in Girls
(Tanner JM, Growth of Adolescence, 1962)
SMR = sexual maturity rating.</p>
<p>SMR Stage Pubic Hair</p>

<p>2 Sparse, lightly pigmented, straight, medial border of labia</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="common-disorders-of-puberty">Common Disorders of Puberty<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-disorders-of-puberty" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Precocious puberty</li>
<li>Delayed puberty</li>
<li>Menstrual abnormalities (amenorrhea, menorrhagia, dysmenorrhea)</li>
<li>Others (infection, neoplasm, hirsutism, etc.)</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="precocious-puberty">PRECOCIOUS PUBERTY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#precocious-puberty" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The term precocious puberty is reserved for girls who exhibit any secondary sex characteristics before the age of 8 or menstruate before the age of 10 .</p>
<p>Precocious puberty may be isosexual where the features are due to excess production of estrogen.</p>
<p>It may be heterosexual where features are due to excess production of androgen (from ovarian and adrenal neoplasm).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="forms-of-precocious-puberty">FORMS OF PRECOCIOUS PUBERTY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#forms-of-precocious-puberty" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>GnRH dependentâ€”80% (complete, central, isosexual or true)
Constitutionalâ€”most common
Juvenile primary hypothyroidism
Intracranial lesions-trauma, tumor or infection</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="incomplete">Incomplete<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#incomplete" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-of-precocious-puberty">CAUSES OF PRECOCIOUS PUBERTY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-precocious-puberty" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">DIAGNOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>History
Basic investigations
X-ray, ct scan, MRI
Serum hCG, FSH, LH
Thyroid profile (TSH, T4)
Serum estradiol, testosterone, 17 OH progesterone, dehydroepiandrosterone (DHEA).</p>
<p>Electroencephalogram.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">TREATMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-goals-are">The goals are:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-goals-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To reduce gonadotropin secretions.
To suppress gonadal steroidogenesis or counteract the peripheral action of sex steroids.</p>
<p>To decrease the growth rate to normal and slowing the skeletal maturation.
To protect the girl from sex abuse.
DRUG MNX</p>
<p>GnRH agonist therapy arrests the pubertal precocity and growth velocity significantly.</p>
<p>The agonists suppress the premature activation of hypothalamopituitary axis due to down regulation and thereby diminished estrogen secretion.</p>
<p>GnRH agonist therapy is the drug of choice in cases with GnRH dependent precocious puberty.</p>
<p>GnRH agonist therapy suppresses FSH, IH secretion, reverses the ovarian cycle, establishes amenorrhea, causes regression of breast, pubic hair changes, and other secondary sexual characteristics.</p>
<p>This drug should be continued till the median age of puberty</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="gnrh-agonist">GnRH agonist<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gnrh-agonist" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Buserelin nasal spray 100 mg daily. It can slow down the process of skeletal maturation</li>
<li>Medroxyprogesterone acetate-30 mg daily orally or 100-200 mg. IM weekly to suppress gonadal steroids. It can suppress menstruation and breast development but cannot change the skeletal growth rate.</li>
<li>Cyproterone acetate-It acts as a potent progestogen, having agonist effects on progesterone receptors.</li>
</ul>
<p>Dose-70-100 mg/m2/day orally for 10 days starting from 5th day of cycle.
4. Danazol-It produces amenorrhea and arrest breast development. But there is no effect on growth rate or skeletal maturation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-delayed-puberty">2. DELAYED PUBERTY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-delayed-puberty" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Puberty is said to be delayed when the breast tissue and/or pubic hair have not appeared by 13-14 years or menarche appears as late as 16 years.</p>
<p>The normal upper age limit of menarche is 15 years.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-of-delayed-puberty">CAUSES OF DELAYED PUBERTY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-delayed-puberty" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypergonadotropic hypogonadism</li>
</ul>
<p>Gonadal dysgenesis, 45 XO
Pure gonadal dysgenesis <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>46</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">X</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">X</mi></mrow><mo separator="true">,</mo><mn>46</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">X</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">Y</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">46 \mathrm{XX}, 46 \mathrm{XY}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8778em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">46</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">XX</span></span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord">46</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.025em;">XY</span></span></span></span></span></span></p>

2. Hypogonadotropic hypogonadism</p>
<p>Constitutional delay

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="menstrual-cycle">Menstrual cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#menstrual-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A periodic physiologic vaginal hemorrhage, occurring at approximately <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>28</mn><mo>Â±</mo><mn>7</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">28 \pm 7</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">28</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">Â±</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">7</span></span></span></span></span> days interval (from the start of one menstrual period to the start of the next), and having its source from the shedding of uterine mucous membrane (menstruation); usually the bleeding is preceded by ovulation and predecidual changes in the endometrium.</p>
<p>This may be teleologically regarded as periodic preparations for fertilization and pregnancy.</p>
<p>Menstruation is the visible manifestation of cyclic physiologic uterine bleeding due to shedding of the endometrium following invisible interplay of hormones mainly through hypothalamo-pituitaryovarian axis.</p>
<p>For the menstruation to occur, the axis must be actively coordinated, endometrium must be responsive to the ovarian hormones (estrogen and progesterone) and the outflow tract must be patent.</p>
<p>The first menstruation (menarche) occurs between 11-15 years with a mean of 13 years. It is more closely related to bone age than to chronological age</p>
<p>For the past couple of decades, the age of menarche is gradually declining with improvement of nutrition and environmental condition.</p>
<p>Physiologically, it is kept in abeyance due to pregnancy and lactation
Women have around 400 menstrual cycles during the course of their lifetimes
Ultimately, it ceases between the ages 45-50 when menopause sets in
The duration of menstruation (menses) is about 4-5 days and the amount of blood loss is estimated to be 20 to 80 mL with an average of 35 mL .</p>
<p>Nearly 70% of total menstrual blood loss occurs in the first 2 days.
The menstrual discharge consists mainly of:
dark altered blood,
mucus,
vaginal epithelial cells,
fragments of endometrium,
prostaglandins,
enzymes and bacteria.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prenatal-follicular-development">Prenatal follicular development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prenatal-follicular-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>During intrauterine fetal development, the ovary develops through 3 stages;
Genital ridge stage - Sex cells can first be identified and begin as hypertrophy of the coelomic epithelium (future peritoneum) overlying the developing mesonephroi. Further growth of the ridges is dependent upon the arrival of germ cells.</p>
<p>Indifferent stage - Proliferation of germinal cells by mitosis and somatic cells
Sexual differentiation stage - Fundamental histologic differences between the ovary and testis are established</p>
<p>To maintain species-specific chromosome complement;</p>
<ul>
<li>the male gametes go through meiosis after puberty and continues throughout life owing to persistence of mitotically active "stem cells", (spermatogonia)</li>
<li>the female gametes undergo meiosis during fetal life and all stem cells are eliminated during birth when meiosis is suspended in the middle of the first meiotic division to resume shortly before ovulation in response to LH surge</li>
</ul>
<p>The normal human menstrual cycle can be divided into two segments:</p>
<ul>
<li>the ovarian cycle and</li>
<li>the uterine cycle, based on the organ under examination</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-ovarian-cycle">The ovarian cycle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-ovarian-cycle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Def: is the cyclic hormonal changes and other series of changes that occur in the ovary to mature the immature follicle and recruit the oocyte.</p>
<p>It may be further divided into:
Follicular phase extends from the beginning of menstruation (day 1) to the onset of ovulation. The average length of the human follicular phase ranges from 10 to 14 days, and variability in this length is responsible for most variations in total cycle length.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ovulation">Ovulation.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ovulation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>luteal phase (post ovulstory phase) extends from ovulation to the beginning of menstruation. Unlike the follicular phase this phase is most predictable and constant (14 days) in length</p>
<p>Ovarian cycle
the ovarian cycle consists of:
Follicular phase:
Recruitment of groups of follicles
Selection of dominant follicle and its maturation.
Ovulation
Luteal phase:
Corpus luteum formation
Demise of the corpus luteum.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="recruitment-of-groups-of-follicles-preantral-phase">Recruitment of groups of follicles (Preantral phase)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#recruitment-of-groups-of-follicles-preantral-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The cohort of the growing follicles undergoes a process of development and differentiation which takes about 85 days and spreads over 3 ovarian cycles.</p>
<p>It is not clear as to how many and which of the primordial follicles amidst several thousands are recruited for a particular cycle.</p>
<p>It is presumed that about 20 antral follicles (about 5-10 per ovary) proceed to develop in each cycle.</p>
<p>The initial recruitment and growth of primordial follicles are not under the control of any hormone.</p>
<p>After a certain stage ( <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>2</mn><mo>âˆ’</mo><mn>5</mn><mrow><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">2-5 \mathrm{~mm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">2</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">âˆ’</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">5</span><span class="mord"><span class="mspace nobreak">&nbsp;</span><span class="mord mathrm">mm</span></span></span></span></span></span> in size), the growth and differentiation of primordial follicles are under the control of FSH.</p>
<p>Unless the follicles are rescued by FSH at this stage, they undergo atresia.</p>
<p>With FSH, the oocyte is now surrounded by an acellular barrier of glycoprotein produced by the follicular cells and is called zona pellucida.</p>
<p>The flattened outer single layer pregranulosa cells become cuboidal and multilayered â€”now called granulosa cells</p>
<p>Then, there is appearance of channels (gap junctions) between the granulosa cells and the oocyte.</p>
<p>Through these gap junctions nutrition to the oocyte is maintained.
There is noticeable beginning of differentiation of the theca interna layer of ovarian stroma surrounding the follicle.</p>
<p>The granulosa cells now acquire FSH receptors.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="antrum-formation">Antrum formation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antrum-formation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Then, there is accelerated growth of all the components of the follicles of the prentral phase.</p>
<p>The granulosa cells grow faster than the theca cells.
There is production of follicular fluid which is primarily an ultrafiltrate of blood from the vessels within theca interna.</p>
<p>The fluidfilled space is formed amidst the granulosa cells.</p>
<p>The spaces coalesce to form an antrum</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dominant-follicle">Dominant Follicle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dominant-follicle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>As early as day 5-7, one of the follicles out of so many becomes dominant and undergoes further maturation.</p>
<p>It seems probable that the one with highest antral concentration of estrogen and lowest androgen and whose granulosa cells contain the maximum receptors for FSH, becomes the dominant follicle.</p>
<p>The rest of the follicles become atretic by day 8
Further growth of dominant follicle
There is marked enlargement of the granulosa cells.
The granulosa cells surround the ovum to form cumulus oophorus which infact anchors the ovum to the wall of the follicle.</p>
<p>The cells adjacent to the ovum are arranged radially and is called corona radiata.
At this stage, FSH induces LH receptors on the granulosa cells of the dominant follicle.</p>
<p>LH receptor induction is essential for the mid-cycle LH surge to induce ovulation, luteinization of the granulosa cells to form corpus luteum and secretion of progesterone (two cell, two gonadotropin therapy)</p>
<p>Mature Graafian follicle</p>
<p>The fully mature Graafian follicle just prior to ovulation measures about 20 mm , and is composed of the following structures from outside inward:</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mspace width="1em"></mspace></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\quad</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 1em;"></span></span></span></span></span> Theca externa.</li>
<li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mspace width="1em"></mspace></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\quad</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 1em;"></span></span></span></span></span> Theca interna.</li>
<li>Membrana granulosa (limitans).</li>
<li>Granulosa cell layer.</li>
<li>Discus proligerus in which the ovum is incorporated with cells arranged radially (corona radiata).</li>
<li>Antrum containing vesicular fluid.</li>
</ul>
<p>it takes 3 months for the follicle to grow and mature to ovulation-2 months to reach an antral stage measuring 1 mm ; 2 weeks to reach 5 mm and another 2 weeks to reach 20 mm before ovulation.</p>
<p>Hormonal changes during follicular phase of ovarian cycle...
At the start of the menstrual cycle, FSH levels begin to rise as the pituitary is released from the negative feedback effects of progesterone, oestrogen and inhibin.</p>
<p>Rising FSH levels rescue a cohort of follicles from atresia, and initiate steroidogenesis.</p>
<p>Under influence of FSH, a cavity forms around the ovum (antrum formation).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nb-on-steroidogenesis">NB. On steroidogenesis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nb-on-steroidogenesis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The basis of hormonal activity in pre-antral to pre-ovulatory follicles is described as the 'two cell, two gonadotrophin' hypothesis.</p>
<p>Steroidogenesis is compartmentalized in the two cell types within the follicle: the theca and granulosa cells.</p>
<p>The two cell, two gonadotrophin hypothesis states that these cells are responsive to the gonadotrophins LH and FSH respectively.</p>
<p>Within the theca cells, LH stimulates the production of androgens from cholesterol.</p>
<p>Within the granulosa cells, FSH stimulates the conversion of thecally derived androgens to oestrogens (aromatization).</p>
<p>In addition to its effects on aromatization, FSH is also responsible for the proliferation of granulosa cells.</p>
<p>Androgen production within the follicle regulate the development of the pre-antral follicle.</p>
<p>Low levels of androgens enhance aromatization and therefore increase oestrogen production.</p>
<p>In contrast, high androgen levels inhibit aromatization and produce follicular atresia.</p>
<p>A delicate balance of FSH and LH is required for early follicular development.</p>
<p>The ideal situation for the initial stages of follicular development is low LH levels and high FSH levels, as seen in the early menstrual cycle.</p>
<p>If LH levels are too high, theca cells produce large amounts of androgens, causing follicular atresia.</p>
<p>The selection of the dominant follicle is the result of complex signalling between the ovary and the pituitary.</p>
<p>Such a follicle has the most efficient aromatase activity and the highest concentration of FSH-induced LH receptors.</p>
<p>The dominant follicle therefore produces the greatest amount of oestradiol and inhibin.</p>
<p>Inhibin further amplifies LH-induced androgen synthesis, which is used as a substrate for oestradiol synthesis.</p>
<p>These features mean that the largest follicle therefore requires the lowest levels of FSH (and LH) for continued development.</p>
<p>At the time of follicular selection, FSH levels are declining in response to the negative-feedback effects of oestrogen.</p>
<p>The dominant follicle is therefore the only follicle that is capable of continued development in the face of falling FSH levels.
in-vitro fertilization (IVF) &amp; multiple pregnancy
During in-vitro fertilization (IVF), the production of many ovulatory follicles is desired to harvest many oocytes.
with the administration of exogenous gonadotrophins, many follicles continue to develop and are released at ovulation, with an ensuing multiple gestation rate of around <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>30</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">30 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">30%</span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p>INHIBIN &amp; ACTIVIN
Granulosa cell inhibin enhances LH -induced androgen synthesis.
The production of inhibin is a further mechanism by which FSH levels are reduced below a threshold at vlhich only the dominant follicle can respond, ensuring atresia of the remaining follicles.</p>
<p>Activin augments pituitary FSH secretion and increases FSH binding to granulosa cells.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ovulation">Ovulation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ovulation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The dominant follicle, shortly before ovulation reaches the surface of the ovary.
The cumulus becomes detached from the wall, so that the ovum with the surrounding cells (corona radiata) floats freely in the liquor folliculi.</p>
<p>The oocyte completes the first meiotic division with extrusion of the first polar body which is pushed away.</p>
<p>The follicular wall near the ovarian surface becomes thinner.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hormonal-changes-at-ovulation">Hormonal changes at ovulation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hormonal-changes-at-ovulation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As the dominant follicle develops further, follicular oestrogen production increases.</p>
<p>Eventually the production of oestrogen is sufficient for it to reach the threshold required to exert a positive-feedback effect on pituitary LH secretion</p>
<p>LH levels increase, at first quite slowly (day 8 to day 12 of the menstrual cycle) and then more rapidly (day 12 onwards).</p>
<p>Hormonal changes at ovulation..
During this time, LH induces luteinization of granulosa cells in the dominant follicle, so that progesterone is produced.</p>
<p>Progesterone further amplifies the positive-feedback effect of oestrogen on pituitary LH secretion, leading to a surge of LH.</p>
<p>Ovulation occurs 36 hours after the onset of the LH surge.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hormonal-changes-at-ovulation">Hormonal changes at ovulation...<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hormonal-changes-at-ovulation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In addition to the rise in LH, FSH and oestrogen that occurs around ovulation, a rise in serum androgen levels also occurs.</p>
<p>These androgens are derived from the stimulatory effect of LH on theca cells, particularly those of the non-dominant follicle.</p>
<p>This rise in androgens may have an important physiological effect in the stimulation of libido, ensuring that sexual activity is likely to occur at the time of ovulation, when the woman is at her most fertile and enhance the process of atresia of the small follicles.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hormonal-changes-at-ovulation">Hormonal changes at ovulation...<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hormonal-changes-at-ovulation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Prior to the release of the oocyte at the time of ovulation, the LH surge stimulates the resumption of meiosis, a process which is completed after the sperm enters the egg (fertilization)</p>
<p>Hormonal changes at ovulation...
Additionally, the LH surge stimulates increased follicular leukocytes eg macrophage chemotactic protein-1 (MCP-I), interleukin 8 (IL-8) &amp; neutrophils into the preovulatory follicle.</p>
<p>Once activated, these leukocytes secrete mediators which cause the follicle wall to break down, releasing the oocyte at ovulation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="luteal-phase">LUTEAL PHASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#luteal-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Following ovulation, the follicle is changed to corpus luteum.
The ovum is picked up into the fallopian tube and undergoes either degeneration or further maturation, if fertilization occurs.</p>
<p>Menstruation is unrelated to ovulation and anovular menstruation is quite common during adolescence, following childbirth and in women approaching menopause.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="corpus-luteum">Corpus Luteum<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#corpus-luteum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stage-of-proliferation">Stage of Proliferation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stage-of-proliferation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The opening through which the ovum escapes soon becomes plugged with fibrin.
The granulosa cells undergo hypertrophy without multiplication.
The cells become larger, polyhedral with pale vesicular nuclei and frothy cytoplasm.
The cells are called granulosa lutein cells.
The color of thecorpus luteum at this stage is greyish yellow due to presence of lipids</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="corpus-luteum">Corpus luteum..<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#corpus-luteum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stage-of-vascularization">Stage of Vascularization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stage-of-vascularization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Within 24 hours of rupture of the follicle, small capillaries grow into granulosa layer towards the lumen accompanied by lymphatics and fibroblasts.</p>
<p>Extensive vascularization within the corpus luteum ensures that the granulosa cells have a rich blood supply providing the precursors for steroidogenesis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="corpus-luteum">Corpus luteum..<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#corpus-luteum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stage-of-maturation">Stage of Maturation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stage-of-maturation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By 4th day, the luteal cells have attained the maximum size.
Approximately about 7-8 days following ovulation, the corpus luteum attains a size of about <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>1</mn><mo>âˆ’</mo><mn>2</mn><mrow><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1-2 \mathrm{~cm}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">1</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">âˆ’</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">2</span><span class="mord"><span class="mspace nobreak">&nbsp;</span><span class="mord mathrm">cm</span></span></span></span></span></span> and reaches its secretory peak.</p>
<p>The lutein cells become greatly enlarged and develop lipid inclusion, giving the cells a distinctive yellowish color. Cell contain a yellow pigment called lutein</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="corpus-luteum">Corpus luteum<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#corpus-luteum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stage-of-regression">Stage of Regression<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stage-of-regression" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>On the day 22-23 of cycle, retrogression starts.
The first evidence of degeneration is appearance of vacuolation in the cells.
The lutein cells atrophy and the corpus luteum becomes corpus albicans.
Regression of corpus luteum is due to withdrawal of tonic LH support
If, however, fertilization occurs in the particular cycle, regression fails to occur, instead it is converted into corpus luteum of pregnancy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hormonal-changes-in-luteal-phase">Hormonal changes in luteal phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hormonal-changes-in-luteal-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>is characterized by the production of progesterone from the corpus luteum within the ovary.</p>
<p>The production of progesterone from the corpus luteum is dependent on continued pituitary LH secretion.</p>
<p>However, serum levels of progesterone are such that LH and FSH production is relatively suppressed by inhibin.</p>
<p>The <strong>low levels of gonadotrophins</strong> mean that the initiation of <strong>new follicular growth is inhibited</strong> for the duration of the luteal phase.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="hormonal-changes-in-luteal-phase">Hormonal changes in luteal phase<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hormonal-changes-in-luteal-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>In the absence of pregnancy and the production of human chorionic gonadotrophin (hCG) from the implanting embryo, the corpus luteum regresses at the end of the luteal phase, a process known as <strong>luteolysis.</strong></p>
<p>As the corpus luteum dies, <strong>oestrogen, progesterone and inhibin</strong> levels decline.</p>
<p>The pituitary is released from the <strong>negative-feedback</strong> effects of these hormones, and gonadotrophins, particularly FSH, <strong>start to rise</strong>.</p>
<p>A cohort of follicles that happen to be at the pre-antral phase is rescued from atresia and a further menstrual cycle is initiated.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="corpus-luteum-of-pregnancy">Corpus Luteum of Pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#corpus-luteum-of-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>There is a surge of hyperplasia of all the layers between 23rd to 28th day due to chorionic gonadotropin.</p>
<p><strong>hCG, like LH will stimulate</strong> the corpus luteum to secrete progesterone.</p>
<p>The growth reaches its peak at about 8th week when it measures about 2â€“3 cm.</p>
<p>Regression occurs following low levels of chorionic gonadotropin and the degenerative changes take place most frequently at about 6 months of gestation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="corpus-luteum-secretions">Corpus luteum secretions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#corpus-luteum-secretions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Predominantly progesterone is secreted by the corpus luteum to support the endometrium of the luteal phase.</p>
<p>There is also secretion of estrogen, inhibin and relaxin.</p>
<p>Progesterone along with estrogen from corpus luteum maintain the growth of the fertilized ovum.</p>
<p>This is essential till the luteal function is taken over by the placenta.</p>
<p>This turn over of function from corpus luteum of pregnancy to placenta is called <strong>luteal-placental shift.</strong></p>
<p><strong>This transition period continues from seven weeks to ten weeks.</strong></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251214-a881287f.jpeg" alt="img-9.jpeg"></p>
<p>ENDOMETRIUM
The endometrium is the lining epithelium of the uterine cavity above the level of internal os.</p>
<p>It consists of surface epithelium, glands, stroma and blood vessels.
Two distinct divisions are established:-
basal zone (stratum basalis) and
the superficial functional zone.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="basal-layer">BASAL LAYER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#basal-layer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is about one-third of the total depth of the endometrium and lies in contact with the myometrium.</p>
<p>The base of the endometrial glands extends into the layer.
The zone is uninfluenced by hormone and as such, no cyclic changes are observed.
After shedding of the superficial part during menstruation, the regeneration of all the components occurs from this zone. It measures about 1 mm .</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="functional-layer">FUNCTIONAL LAYER<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functional-layer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This zone is under the influence of fluctuating cyclic ovarian hormones, estrogen and progesterone.</p>
<p>The changes in different components during an ovulatory cycle has been traditionally divided into four stages:</p>
<p>Regenerative phase.
Proliferative phase.
Secretory phase.
Menstruation</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stage-of-regeneration">STAGE OF REGENERATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stage-of-regeneration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>starts even before the menstruation ceases and is completed 2-3 days after the end of menstruation.</p>
<p>New blood vessels grow from the stumps of the old one.
The glands and the stromal cells are regenerated from the remnants left in the basal zone.</p>
<p>The glands are lined by the cubical epithelia.
The thickness averages 2 mm .</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stage-of-proliferation">STAGE OF PROLIFERATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stage-of-proliferation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>extends from 5th or 6th day to 14th day (till ovulation).
The proliferative changes occurs due to rise in level of ovarian estrogens.
The glands become tubular and lie perpendicular to the surface.
The epithelium becomes columnar.
Unbranched spiral vessels with capillary congestion
The thickness measures about 3-4 mm.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="secretory-phase">SECRETORY PHASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#secretory-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The changes of the components are due to the combined effects of estrogen and progesterone liberated from the corpus luteum after ovulation.</p>
<p>The endometrium contains receptors for progesterone which are induced by estrogen.</p>
<p>Thus, the progesterone can only act on the endometrium previously primed by estrogen.</p>
<p>It begins on day 15 and ceases 5-6 days prior to menstruation.
The surface epithelium becomes more columnar and ciliated at places.
The glands show predominant changes.
The glands increase in size.
The lining epithelium become taller.
There is appearance of vacuoles due to secretion of glycogen between the nuclei and the basement membrane.</p>
<p>The glands become corkscrew-shaped. The blood vessels undergo marked spiraling.</p>
<p>The thickness of the endometrium reaches its highest (6-8 mm)
The endometrial growth ceases 5-6 days prior to menstruation (22nd or 23rd day of cycle) in an infertile cycle.</p>
<p>The subepithelial capillaries and the spiral vessels are engorged.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="menstrual-phase">MENSTRUAL PHASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#menstrual-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is essentially degeneration and casting off an endometrium prepared for a pregnancy.</p>
<p>Regression of corpus luteum with fall in the level of estrogen and progesterone is an invariable preceding feature</p>
<p>Thes marked spiralling of the arteries and the withdrawal of hormones estrogen and progesterone causes intense spasm of the spiral arterioles at the basal part.</p>
<p>These two lead to stasis and tissue anoxemia.
There are evidences of infiltration of leucocytes and monocytes in the stroma.
Stasis of blood and spasm of the arterioles lead to damage of the arteriolar walls.
There is enzymatic autodigestion of the functional zone.</p>
<p>The bleeding occurs from the broken arteries, veins and capillaries and also from the stromal hematoma, with the superficial functional layer being shed into the uterine cavity</p>
<p>The menstrual flow stops as a result of combined effect of prolonged vasoconstriction, myometrial contraction and local aggregation of platelets with deposition of fibrin around them.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anovular-menstruation">ANOVULAR MENSTRUATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anovular-menstruation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>In an anovulatory cycle, the follicles grow without any selection of dominant follicle. The estrogen is secreted in increasing amount.</p>
<p>There may be imbalance between estrogen and FSH or because of temporary unresponsiveness of the hypothalamus to the rising estrogen, GnRH is suppressed <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>â†’</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\rightarrow</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.3669em;"></span><span class="mrel">â†’</span></span></span></span></span> no ovulation.</p>
<p>The net effect is unopposed secretion of estrogen till the follicles exist.
The endometrium remains in either proliferative or at times hyperplastic state.
When the estrogen level falls, there is asynchronus shedding of the endometrium and menstruation.</p>
<p>The bleeding may be heavy or prolonged and irregular
This type of bleeding is mostly found during adolescence, following childbirth and abortion and in premenopausal period.</p>
