<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="artificial-postponement">ARTIFICIAL POSTPONEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#artificial-postponement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The hormones used for deferment of the period are-combined oral pill, 2 tablets daily or progestogen such as norethisterone 5 mg twice daily.</p>
<p>The drug should be taken at least 3-6 days before the expected date of the period and continued until the crisis is over.</p>
<p>The period is expected 2-3 days after the drug is suspended.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-normal-menstrual-cycle-clinical-features">The normal menstrual cycle-clinical features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-normal-menstrual-cycle-clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>normal menstrual cycle is 28 days +/- 7days
duration of menstrual flow is 3-7 days.
Menstrual cycles are longest immediately after puberty and in the 5 years leading up to the menopause, corresponding to the peak incidence of anovulatory cycles.</p>
<p>The length of the menstrual cycle is determined by the length of the follicular phase.
Once ovulation occurs, luteal phase length is fairly fixed at 14 days in almost all women.</p>
<p>Clinical features
The amount of menstrual flow peaks on the first or second day of menstruation.
The normal volume of menstrual loss is <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn mathvariant="bold">35</mn><mrow><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi mathvariant="bold">m</mi><mi mathvariant="bold">L</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathbf{3 5} \mathbf{~ m L}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6861em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathbf">35</span></span><span class="mord"><span class="mspace nobreak">&nbsp;</span><span class="mord mathbf">mL</span></span></span></span></span></span> per month.
A menstrual loss of greater than 80 mL is considered to be excessive - this level is rather arbitrary and corresponds to the threshold at which iron deficiency anaemia may ensue unless treated.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="new-developments">New developments<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#new-developments" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>IVF - exogenous gonadotrophins are administered to stimulate follicular growth within the ovary</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gnrh-antagonists">GnRH antagonists<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gnrh-antagonists" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gnrh-agonists">GnRH agonists<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gnrh-agonists" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="menstrual-disorders">Menstrual Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#menstrual-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Dysmenorrhea, mittelschmerz's syndrome and Premenstrual syndrome</li>
<li>Abnormal uterine bleeding:</li>
<li>Amenorrhea and Oligomenorrhea</li>
<li>Polycystic ovarian syndrome</li>
<li>Dysfunctional uterine bleeding</li>
<li>Postmenopausal bleeding</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-mittelschmerz-s-syndrome-ovular-pain">1. MITTELSCHMERZ'S SYNDROME (Ovular Pain)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-mittelschmerz-s-syndrome-ovular-pain" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Ovular pain is not an infrequent complaint.</li>
<li>It appears in the midmenstrual period.</li>
<li>The pain is usually situated in the hypogastrium or in either iliac fossa.</li>
<li>The exact cause is not known.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-probable-factors-are">The probable factors are:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-probable-factors-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mspace width="1em"></mspace></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\quad</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 1em;"></span></span></span></span></span> Increased tension of the Graafian follicle just prior to rupture,</li>
<li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mspace width="1em"></mspace></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\quad</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 1em;"></span></span></span></span></span> Peritoneal irritation by the follicular fluid following ovulation and</li>
<li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mspace width="1em"></mspace></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\quad</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0em;"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 1em;"></span></span></span></span></span> Contraction of the tubes and uterus</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-dysmenorrhea">2. DYSMENORRHEA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-dysmenorrhea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Dysmenorrhea literally means painful menstruation.</li>
<li>But a more realistic and practical definition includes cases of painful menstruation of sufficient magnitude so as to incapacitate day-to-day activities.</li>
<li>Prevalence: Dysmenorrhea is a very common complaint, experienced by 45-95 per cent of women of reproductive age.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types">Types:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="primary">Primary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Secondary</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="primary-dysmenorrhea-spasmodic">PRIMARY DYSMENORRHEA (Spasmodic)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-dysmenorrhea-spasmodic" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The primary dysmenorrhea is one where there is no identifiable pelvic pathology.</li>
<li>The incidence of primary dysmenorrhea of sufficient magnitude with incapacitation is about <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>15</mn><mo>âˆ’</mo><mn>20</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">15-20 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">15</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">âˆ’</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">20%</span></span></span></span></span>.</li>
<li>The risk factors for primary dysmenorrhoea include:</li>
<li>duration of menstrual flow of <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>&gt;</mo><mn>5</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">&gt;5</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">&gt;</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">5</span></span></span></span></span> days,</li>
<li>younger than normal age at menarche,</li>
<li>cigarette smoking.</li>
<li>There is some evidence to support the assertion that dysmenorrhoea improves after childbirth, and it also appears to decline with increasing age.</li>
<li>The severity of pain usually lasts for few hours, may extend to 24 hours but seldom persists beyond 48 hours.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="secondary-dysmenorrhea-congestive">SECONDARY DYSMENORRHEA (Congestive)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#secondary-dysmenorrhea-congestive" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>is normally considered to be menstruation - associated pain occurring in the presence of pelvic pathology.</li>
<li>The pain may be related to increasing tension in the pelvic tissues due to premenstrual pelvic congestion or increased vascularity in the pelvic organs.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="common-causes-of-secondary-dysmenorrhea">Common causes of secondary dysmenorrhea:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-causes-of-secondary-dysmenorrhea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>chronic pelvic infection,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pelvic endometriosis,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>adenomyosis</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>pelvic adhesions / Asherman's syndrome</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Uterine fibroid,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>endometrial polyp,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>IUCD in utero</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pelvic congestion.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>(rarely) cervical stenosis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Obstruction due to mullerian malformations</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>NB: some definitions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Endometriosis: Endometrial stroma &amp; glands remote of the uterine cavity, responsive to ovarian hormone variations with fibrosis of surrounding tissues</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sites: Uterine ligaments, bowel, urinary tract, pelvic peritonuem, ovaries, abdominal wall, perineum &amp; vagina.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Adenomyosis/endometriosis interna: Extension of endometrial glands and stroma into the myometrium</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features-of-secondary-dysmenorhea">Clinical features of secondary dysmenorhea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features-of-secondary-dysmenorhea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The pain is dull, situated in the back and in front without any radiation.</li>
<li>It usually appears 3-5 days prior to the period and relieves with the start of bleeding.</li>
<li>The onset and duration of pain depends on the pathology producing the pain.</li>
<li>There is no systemic discomfort unlike primary dysmenorrhea.</li>
<li>The patients may have got some discomfort even in between periods</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-dysmenorhea">Treatment of dysmenorhea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-dysmenorhea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>NSAIDs, such as naproxen, ibuprofen and mefenamic acid, are reasonably effective. Aspirin, Mefenamic acid (500mg TID)</li>
<li>Oral contraceptives are widely used but, surprisingly, there is little evidence.</li>
<li>Surgical treatments aimed at interrupting the nerve pathways from the uterus have been employed</li>
<li>Treat underlying conditions</li>
<li>Conservative mgt; taking a hot bath, using a hot water bottle and relaxing in bed</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-premenstrual-syndrome-pms-syn-premenstrual-tension">3. PREMENSTRUAL SYNDROME (PMS) (Syn : Premenstrual Tension)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-premenstrual-syndrome-pms-syn-premenstrual-tension" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>is the occurrence of cyclical psychoneuroendocrine disorder of unknown etiology, often noticed just prior to menstruation (in luteal phase-premenstrual) and resolve by the time menstruation ceases.</li>
<li>Occur during the last 7-10 days of the menstrual cycle.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="it-should-fulfil-the-following-criteria">It should fulfil the following criteria:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#it-should-fulfil-the-following-criteria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Not related to any organic lesion.</li>
<li>cyclic symptoms occurring only during luteal phase</li>
<li>Symptoms must be severe enough to disturb the lifestyle of the woman or she requires medical help.</li>
<li>Symptom-free period during rest of the cycle.</li>
<li>symptoms relieved with onset of menses</li>
<li>symptoms present for at least 3 cycles</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The exact cause is not known but the following hypotheses are postulated :</p>
<p>(a) Alteration in the level of estrogen and progesterone starting from the midluteal phase. Either there is altered estrogen : progesterone ratio or diminished progesterone level.
(b) Neuroendocrine factors :</p>
<ul>
<li>Serotonin is an important neurotransmitter in the CNS. During the luteal phase, decreased synthesis of serotonin is observed in women suffering from PMS.</li>
<li>Endorphins: The symptom complex of PMS is thought to be due to the withdrawal of endorphins (neurotransmitters) from CNS during the luteal phase.</li>
<li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>Î³</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\gamma</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.625em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.05556em;">Î³</span></span></span></span></span>-aminobutyric acid (GABA) suppresses the anxiety level in the brain. Medications that are GABA agonist, are effective.
(c) Psychological and psychosocial factors may be involved to produce behavioral changes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="unfortunately-nothing-is-conclusive">Unfortunately, nothing is conclusive<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unfortunately-nothing-is-conclusive" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">CLINICAL FEATURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Bloating</li>
<li>cyclical weight gain</li>
<li>Mastalgia</li>
<li>abdominal cramps</li>
<li>Fatigue</li>
<li>Headache</li>
<li>depression</li>
<li>irritability.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-pms">TREATMENT OF PMS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-pms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>As the etiology is multifactorial and too often obscure, various drugs are used either on speculation or empirically with varying degrees of success.</li>
<li>Life style modification and congnitive behavior therapy are important steps.</li>
<li>Nonpharmacological:</li>
<li>Assurance, Yoga, Stress management, Diet manipulation.</li>
<li>Avoidance of salt, caffeine and alcohol specially in second half of cycle improves the symptoms.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nonhormonal">Nonhormonal :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nonhormonal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Tranquilizers or antidepressant drugs, may be of help logically.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pyridoxine 100 mg Bid is helpful by correcting tryptophan metabolism - depression.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diuretics - Frusemide 20 mg OD for consecutive 5 days a week reduces fluid retention.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Anxiolytic agents are found to be helpful to women having persistent anxiety. Alprazolam <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>0.25</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow><mo separator="true">,</mo><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">B</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">I</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">D</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">0.25 \mathrm{mg}, \mathrm{BID}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8778em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">0.25</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">mg</span></span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">BID</span></span></span></span></span></span> ) is given during the luteal phase of the cycle.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Selective Serotonin Reuptake Inhibitors (SSRI) (eg Fluoxetine 20mg) and Noradrenaline Reuptake Inhibitors (SNRI) are found to be very effective.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hormones">Hormones:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hormones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Oral contraceptive pills: The idea is to suppress ovulation and to maintain an uniform hormonal milieu. The therapy is to be continued for <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>3</mn><mo>âˆ’</mo><mn>6</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">3-6</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">3</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">âˆ’</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">6</span></span></span></span></span> cycles.</li>
<li>Progesterone is not effective in treating PMS.</li>
<li>Spironolactone: It is a potassium sparing diuretic. It has antimineralocorticoid and anti-androgenic effects. It is given in the luteal phase ( <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>25</mn><mo>âˆ’</mo><mn>200</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">25-200 \mathrm{mg} /</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">25</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">âˆ’</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">200</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">mg</span></span><span class="mord">/</span></span></span></span></span> day).</li>
<li>Bromocriptine: 2.5 mg daily or twice daily may be helpful, at least to relieve the breast complaints.</li>
<li>Oophorectomy - primary PMS with recurrence of symptoms and approaching to menopause, hysterectomy with bilateral oophorectomy is a last resort</li>
<li>Suppression of ovarian cycle</li>
<li>Medical oopherectomy - GnRH agonist for 6 months</li>
<li>Danazol 200 mg daily is to be adjusted so as to produce amenorrhea</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="menstrual-disorders-abnormal-uterine-bleeding">Menstrual Disorders: Abnormal Uterine Bleeding<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#menstrual-disorders-abnormal-uterine-bleeding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Abnormal Uterine Bleeding
Any uterine bleeding outside the normal volume, duration, regularity or frequency is considered abnormalnuterine bleeding (AUB).</p>
<p>Description of alteration in the normal pattern of menstrual flow
Forms;
Excessive flow
Prolonged flow
Intermenstrual bleeding</p>
<p>Types;</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>hypermenorrhoea - metrorrhagia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>polymenorrhoea - amenorrhoea</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>menometrorrhagia - menorrhagia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>oligomenorrhoea</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-menorrhagia-br-syn-hypermenorrhea">1. MENORRHAGIA &lt;br&gt; (Syn : Hypermenorrhea)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-menorrhagia-br-syn-hypermenorrhea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Menorrhagia is defined as cyclic bleeding at normal intervals; the bleeding is either excessive in amount ( <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>&gt;</mo><mn>80</mn><mrow><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">L</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">&gt;80 \mathrm{~mL}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">&gt;</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6833em;"></span><span class="mord">80</span><span class="mord"><span class="mspace nobreak">&nbsp;</span><span class="mord mathrm">mL</span></span></span></span></span></span> ) or duration ( <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>&gt;</mo><mn>7</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">&gt;7</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">&gt;</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">7</span></span></span></span></span> days) or both.</p>
<p>The term menotaxis is often used to denote prolonged bleeding.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-of-menorrhagia">Classification of menorrhagia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-menorrhagia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Menorrhagia can be classified as:
idiopathic, where no organic pathology can be found: also known as dysfunctional uterine bleeding-(DUB).
secondary to an organic cause, such as fibroids.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-organic">1. Organic:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-organic" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a. Pelvic causes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Fibroid uterus</li>
<li>Adenomyosis</li>
<li>Pelvic endometriosis</li>
<li>IUCD inutero</li>
<li>Chronic tubo-ovarian mass</li>
<li>Tubercular endometritis (early cases)</li>
<li>Retroverted uterus-due to congestion</li>
<li>Granulosa cell tumor of the ovary</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-systemic">b. Systemic:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-systemic" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Liver dysfunction-failure to conjugate and thereby inactivates the estrogens.</p>
<ul>
<li>Congestive cardiac failure.</li>
<li>Severe hypertension</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-endocrinal">c. Endocrinal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-endocrinal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypothyroidism.</li>
<li>Hyperthyroidism.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="d-hematological">d. <div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-functional">2. Functional<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-functional" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>

</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="common-causes-of-menorrhagia">COMMON CAUSES OF MENORRHAGIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-causes-of-menorrhagia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Dysfunctional uterine bleeding</li>
<li>Fibroid uterus</li>
<li>Adenomyosis</li>
<li>Chronic tubo-ovarian mass</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis-treatment">Diagnosis &amp; treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>number of towels and tampons used per day is useful</li>
<li>irregular, intermenstrual or postcoital bleeding, a sudden change in symptoms, dyspareunia, pelvic pain or premenstrual pain, and excessive bleeding from other sites or in other situations (e.g. after tooth extraction).</li>
<li>Long duration of flow, passage of big clots, use of increased number of thick sanitary pads, pallor, and low level of hemoglobin give an idea about the correct diagnosis and magnitude of menorrhagia.</li>
</ul>
<p>Treatment: The definitive treatment is appropriate to the cause for menorrhagia.
Some Definitive Treatment
Drugs that are compatible with ongoing attempts at conception</p>
<ul>
<li>Mefenamic acid and other non-steroidal, anti-inflammatory drugs (NSAIDs)</li>
<li>Tranexamic acid</li>
<li>Drugs that are incompatible with ongoing attempts at conception but not licensed for use as contraceptives</li>
<li>Danazol</li>
<li>used as contraceptives that are effective in the treatment of menorrhagia</li>
<li>Combined oral contraceptive pill</li>
<li>levonorgestrel intrauterine system.</li>
<li>Second-line drugs with few advantages over the forgoing, and whose side effects limit long-term use</li>
<li>Danazol</li>
<li>Gestrinone</li>
<li>Gonadotrophin-releasing hormone analogues</li>
<li>Medical and surgical treatments that are not effective in the treatment of menorrhagia</li>
<li>Ethamsylate</li>
<li>Luteal phase progestogens</li>
<li>Uterine curettage</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="surgical-treatments-for-menorrhagia">Surgical treatments for menorrhagia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-treatments-for-menorrhagia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>ablation of the endometrial lining of the uterus to sufficient depth prevents regeneration of the endometrium.</li>
<li>Hysterectomy</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-polymenorrhea-syn-epimenorrhea">2. POLYMENORRHEA (SYN : EPIMENORRHEA)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-polymenorrhea-syn-epimenorrhea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>is defined as cyclic bleeding where the cycle is reduced to an arbitrary limit of less than 21 days and remains constant at that frequency.</li>
<li>If the frequent cycle is associated with excessive and or prolonged bleeding, it is called epimenorrhagia.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-treatment">Causes &amp; treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dysfunctional">Dysfunctional:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dysfunctional" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is seen predominantly during adolescence, preceding menopause and following delivery and abortion.</li>
<li>Hyperstimulation of the ovary by the pituitary hormones may be the responsible factor.</li>
</ul>
<p>Ovarian hyperemia as in PID or ovarian endometriosis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Persistent dysfunctional type is to be treated by hormone as in DUB</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-metrorrhagia">3. METRORRHAGIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-metrorrhagia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>is defined as irregular, acyclic bleeding from the uterus.</li>
<li>Amount of bleeding is variable.</li>
<li>While metrorrhagia strictly concerns uterine bleeding but in clinical practice, the bleeding from any part of the genital tract is included under the heading.</li>
<li>Then again, irregular bleeding in the form of contact bleeding or intermenstrual bleeding in an otherwise normal cycle is also included in metrorrhagia.</li>
<li>In fact, it is mostly related to surface lesion in the uterus.</li>
</ul>
<p>Menometrorrhagia is the term applied when the bleeding is so irregular and excessive that the menses (periods) cannot be identified at all.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-of-acyclic-bleeding">CAUSES OF ACYCLIC BLEEDING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-acyclic-bleeding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>DUBâ€”usually during adolescence, following childbirth and abortion and preceding menopause</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Submucous fibroid</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Uterine polyp</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Carcinoma cervix and endometrial carcinoma</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes-of-contact-bleeding">CAUSES OF CONTACT BLEEDING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-contact-bleeding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Carcinoma cervix</li>
<li>Mucos polyp of cervix</li>
<li>Vascular ectopy of the cervix especially during pregnancy, pill use cervix</li>
<li>Infections-chlamydial or tubercular cervicitis</li>
<li>Cervical endometriosis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-of-intermenstrual-bleeding">CAUSES OF INTERMENSTRUAL BLEEDING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-intermenstrual-bleeding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Apart from the causes of contact bleeding, other causes are:</li>
<li>Urethral caruncle</li>
<li>Ovular bleeding</li>
<li>Breakthrough bleeding in pill use</li>
<li>IUCD in utero</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-metrorhagia">Treatment of metrorhagia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-metrorhagia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Treatment is directed to the underlying pathology.
Malignancy is to be excluded prior to any definitive treatmentecubitus ulcer</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-oligomenorrhea">4. OLIGOMENORRHEA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-oligomenorrhea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Definition: Menstrual bleeding occurring more than 35 days apart and which remains constant at that frequency is called oligomenorrhea.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="common-causes-of-oligomenorrhea">COMMON CAUSES OF OLIGOMENORRHEA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-causes-of-oligomenorrhea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Age-relatedâ€”during adolescence and preceeding menopause</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Weight-relatedâ€”obesity</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stress and exercise related</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Endocrine disordersâ€”PCOS (commonest), hyperprolactinemia, hyperthyroidism</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Androgen producing tumors-ovarian, adrenal</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Tubercular endometritisâ€”late cases</p>
</li>

<p>Drugs:</p>
</li>
