<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="5-amenorrhoea">5. AMENORRHOEA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-amenorrhoea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>absence of menstruation.</li>
<li>It may be classified as either primary or secondary.</li>
<li>There are, physiological situations in which amenorrhoea is normal, namely:</li>
<li>pregnancy,</li>
<li>lactation and</li>
<li>prior to the onset of puberty.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-of-amenorrhoea">Classification of amenorrhoea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-amenorrhoea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Primary amenorrhoea: condition in which girls fail to develop secondary sexual characteristics by 14 years of age or fail to menstruate by 16 years of age.</li>
<li>Secondary amenorrhoea: describes the cessation of menstruation for more than 6 months in a normal female of reproductive age that is not due to pregnancy.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-of-amenorrhoea">Causes of amenorrhoea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-amenorrhoea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Reproductive outflow tract disorders</li>
<li>Asherman 's syndrome</li>
<li>Mullerian agenesis</li>
<li>Transverse vaginal septum</li>
<li>Imperforate hymen</li>
<li>Testicular feminization syndrome</li>
<li>Ovarian disorders</li>
<li>Anovulation, e.g. polycystic ovarian synd rome (peaS)</li>
<li>Gonadal dysgenesis, e.g. Turner's syndrome</li>
<li>Premature ovarian failure</li>
<li>Resistant ovary syndrome</li>
<li>Pituitary disorders</li>
<li>Adenomas such as prolactinoma</li>
<li>Pituitary necrosis, e.g. Sheehan's syndrome</li>
<li>Hypothalamic malfunctions</li>
<li>Resulting from excessive exercise</li>
<li>Resulting from weight loss/anorexia nervosa</li>
<li>Resulting from stress</li>
<li>Craniopharyngioma</li>
<li>Kallman 's syndrome</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis-treatment">Diagnosis &amp; treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Detailed history and examination</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Investigations</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Initial hormone tests:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pregnancy test,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prolactin,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Thyroid function,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>LH and FSH,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Testosterone - androgen producing tumours</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Treat the cause.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="6-hypomenorrhea">6. HYPOMENORRHEA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-hypomenorrhea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Definition: When the menstrual bleeding is unduly scanty and lasts for less than 2 days, it is called hypomenorrhea.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The causes may be:</li>
<li>local (uterine synechiae or endometrial tuberculosis),</li>
<li>endocrinal (use of oral contraceptives, thyroid dysfunction, and premenopausal period), or systemic (malnutrition).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-dysfunctional-uterine-bleeding-dub">7. DYSFUNCTIONAL UTERINE BLEEDING (DUB)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-dysfunctional-uterine-bleeding-dub" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>DUB is defined as a state of abnormal uterine bleeding without any clinically detectable organic, systemic, and iatrogenic cause (Pelvic pathology, e.g. tumor, inflammation or pregnancy is excluded).</li>
<li>NB: Heavy menstrual bleeding (HMB) is defined as a bleeding that interferes with woman's physical, emotional, social and maternal quality of life.</li>
</ul>
<p>DUB</p>
<ul>
<li>The bleeding may be abnormal in frequency, amount, or duration or combination of any three.</li>
<li>As the diagnosis is based with the exclusion of 'organic
lesion', Currently DUB is defined as a state of abnormal uterine bleeding following anovulation due to dysfunction of hypothalamo-pituitary-ovarian axis (endocrine origin).</li>
</ul>
<p>Pathophysiology</p>
<ul>
<li>The endometrial abnormalities may be primary or secondary to incoordination in the hypothalamopituitary- ovarian axis.</li>
<li>It is thus more prevalent in extremes of reproductive periodâ€”adolescence and premenopause or following childbirth and abortion.</li>
<li>The abnormal bleeding may be associated with or without ovulation and accordingly grouped into :</li>
<li>Ovular bleeding</li>
<li>Anovular bleeding</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ovular-bleeding">OVULAR BLEEDING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ovular-bleeding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Polymenorrhea or polymenorrhagia:</li>
<li>usually occurs following childbirth and abortion, during adolescence and premenopausal period, and in pelvic inflammatory disease.</li>
<li>The follicular development is speeded up with resulting shortening of the follicular phase.</li>
<li>This is probably due to hyperstimulation of the follicular growth by FSH.</li>
<li>Rarely, the luteal phase may be shortened due to premature lysis of the corpus luteum.</li>
<li>Sometimes, it is related to stress induced stimulation.</li>
<li>Oligomenorrhea:</li>
<li>Primary ovular oligomenorrhea is rare.</li>
<li>Common in adolescence and premenopause.</li>
<li>The disturbance may be due to ovarian unresponsiveness to FSH or secondary to pituitary dysfunction.</li>
<li>There is undue prolongation of the proliferative phase with normal secretory phase.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="anovular-bleeding">ANOVULAR BLEEDING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anovular-bleeding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Menorrhagia</li>
<li>Anovular bleeding is usually excessive.</li>
<li>In the absence of growth limiting progesterone due to anovulation, the endometrial growth is under the influence of estrogen throughout the cycle.</li>
<li>There is inadequate structural stromal support and the endometrium remains fragile.</li>
<li>Thus, with the withdrawal of estrogen due to negative feedback action of FSH, the endometrial shedding continues for a longer period in asynchronous sequences because of lack of compactness</li>
<li>Cystic glandular hyperplasia</li>
<li>This type of abnormal bleeding is usually met in premenopausal women</li>
<li>There is slow increase in secretion of estrogen but no negative feedback inhibition of FSH.</li>
<li>The net effect is gradual rise in the level of estrogen with concomittant phase of amenorrhea for about 6-8 weeks.</li>
<li>As there is no ovulation, the endometrium is under the influence of estrogen without being opposed by growth limiting progesterone for a prolonged period.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>History, physical examination &amp; Investigations aim at:</li>
<li>To confirm the menstrual abnormality as stated by the patient.</li>
<li>To exclude the systemic, iatrogenic, and 'organic' pelvic pathology.</li>
<li>To identify the possible etiology of DUB.</li>
<li>To work out the definite therapy protocol.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Because of diverse etiopathology of DUB in different phases of woman's life, the management protocols have been grouped accordingly.
o Pubertal and adolescent menorrhagia <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>&lt;</mo><mn>20</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">&lt;20</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">&lt;</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">20</span></span></span></span></span> years.
o Reproductive period (20-40 years).
o Premenopausal (&gt; 40 years).
o Postmenopausal.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general">General<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Rest is advised during bleeding phase.</li>
<li>Assurance and sympathetic handling are helpful particularly in adolescents.</li>
<li>Anemia should be corrected energetically by diet, hematinics, and even by blood transfusion.</li>
<li>Clinically evident systemic or endocrinal abnormalities should be investigated and treated accordingly.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="medical">MEDICAL<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>potent orally active progestins, are the mainstay in the management of DUB in all age groups.</li>
<li>Mechanism of antiestrogenic action of progestins are:
o <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>â‹…</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\cdot</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">â‹…</span></span></span></span></span> It stimulates the enzyme (17- <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>Î²</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\beta</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.05278em;">Î²</span></span></span></span></span>-hydroxy steroid
dehydrogenase) that converts estradiol to estrone (less potent).
o ãƒ» Inhibits induction of estrogen receptor.
o ãƒ» It has antimitotic effect on the endometrium.</li>
<li>While isolated progestins therapy is highly effective in anovular DUB, in ovular DUB combined preparations of progestogen and estrogen (combined oral pills) are effective.</li>
<li>To stop bleeding and regulate the cycle : Norethisterone preparations (5 mg tab) are used thrice daily till bleeding stops, which it usually does by 3-7 days.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cyclic-therapy">Cyclic Therapy:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cyclic-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>In ovular bleeding, Any low dose combined oral pills are effective when given 5th to 25th day of cycle for 3 consecutive cycles. It causes endometrial atrophy. It is more effective compared to progesterone therapy as it suppress the hypothalamopituitary axis more effectively. Normal menstruation is expected to resume with restoration of normally functioning pituitary-ovarian-endometrial axis</li>
<li>In anovular bleeding: Cyclic progestogen preparation of medroxyprogesterone acetate (MPA) 10 mg or norethisterone 5 mg is used from 5th to 25th day of cycle for 3 cycles</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="non-hormonal-management">NON-HORMONAL MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#non-hormonal-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Anti-fibrinolytic agents - Tranexamic acid</li>
<li>Prostaglandin synthetase inhibitors: eg Mefenamic acid 150-600mg is much effective in women aged more than 35 years and in cases of ovulatory DUB during bleeding phase.</li>
<li>Desmopressin: It is a synthetic analogue of arginine-vasopressin. indicated in von Willebrand's disease and factor VIII deficiency. It is given IV <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>0.3</mn><mi>Î¼</mi><mrow><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">k</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">(0.3 \mu \mathrm{~g} / \mathrm{kg})</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">0.3</span><span class="mord mathnormal">Î¼</span><span class="mord"><span class="mspace nobreak">&nbsp;</span><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">g</span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">kg</span></span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span> or intranasally.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="surgical-management-of-dub">SURGICAL MANAGEMENT OF DUB<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-management-of-dub" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Uterine curettage</li>
<li>Endometrial ablation/resection</li>
<li>Hysterectomy</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="8-polycystic-ovarian-syndrome">8. POLYCYSTIC OVARIAN SYNDROME<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#8-polycystic-ovarian-syndrome" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>is a syndrome of ovarian dysfunction along with the cardinal features of hyperandrogenism and polycystic ovary morphology.</li>
<li>PCOS remains a syndrome, and as such no single diagnostic criterion (such as hyperandrogenism or polycystic ovary) is sufficient for clinical diagnosis.</li>
<li>Its clinical manifestations may include:</li>
<li>menstrual irregularities,</li>
<li>signs of androgen excess</li>
<li>obesity.</li>
<li>Insulin resistance</li>
<li>elevated serum LH levels.</li>
<li>PCOS is associated with an increased risk of type 2 diabetes and cardiovascular events.</li>
</ul>
<p>Prevalence:</p>
<ul>
<li>affects around 5-10% of women of reproductive age.</li>
<li>The prevalence of polycystic ovaries seen on ultrasound is much higher around <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>25</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">25 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">25%</span></span></span></span></span>.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aetiology">Aetiology:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aetiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>remains unclear but is self-perpetuating once starts.</li>
<li>Women with this syndrome have increased ovarian androgen due partly to disordered ovarian cytochrome P450 activity and partly to increased LH stimulation.</li>
<li>Additionally, increasing evidence suggests a role for (peripheral) insulin resistance in the pathophysiology, with the resulting hyperinsulinaemia also promoting ovarian androgen production.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features">Clinical features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Oligomenorrhoea/amenorrhoea: this occurs in up to 65-75% and is predominantly related to chronic anovulation.</li>
<li>Hirsutism: this occurs in 30-70%.</li>
<li>Subfertility: up to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>75</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">75 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">75%</span></span></span></span></span> of women with PCOS who try to conceive have difficulty doing so.</li>
<li>Obesity: at least <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>40</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">40 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">40%</span></span></span></span></span> are clinically obese.</li>
<li>Recurrent miscarriage: is seen in 50-60% of women with more than three early pregnancy losses.</li>
<li>Acanthosis nigricans: areas of increased skin pigmentation that are velvety in texture and occur in the axillae and other flexures occur in around 2% of women with PCOS.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Elevated testosterone levels. <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>=</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">=</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.3669em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span></span></span></span></span> testosterone &amp; androstenedione</li>
<li>Decreased sex hormone binding globulin (SHBG) levels.</li>
<li>Elevated LH levels.</li>
<li>Elevated LH:FSH ratio. Typically LH:FSH &gt; 2:3.1</li>
<li>Increased fasting insulin levels.</li>
<li>Free testosterone is higher than normal, since SHBG levels are low. Testosterone levels of <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>&gt;</mo><mn>5</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">n</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">o</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">l</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">L</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">&gt;5 \mathrm{nmol} / \mathrm{L}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">&gt;</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">5</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">nmol</span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord mathrm">L</span></span></span></span></span> should prompt a search for an androgensecreting tumour.</li>
<li>Transvaginal U/S:</li>
<li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>â‰¥</mo><mn>10</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\geq 10</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7719em; vertical-align: -0.136em;"></span><span class="mrel">â‰¥</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">10</span></span></span></span></span> peripheral cysts btn 2-8 mm diameter ('string of pearls' sign)</li>
<li>Increased ovarian stromal volume to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>&gt;</mo><mn>8</mn><msup><mrow><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi mathvariant="normal">c</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow><mn>3</mn></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">&gt;8 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">&gt;</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8141em;"></span><span class="mord">8</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"><span class="mspace nobreak">&nbsp;</span><span class="mord mathrm">cm</span></span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8141em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">3</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-pcos">Management of PCOS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-pcos" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Aim of Rx depends on main complaint</p>
<ul>
<li>Weight loss</li>
<li>Cyclic progestagens or limited use of COC (menstrual disturbance)</li>
<li>Anti-androgens; cyproterone acetate, spironolactone,</li>
<li>cosmetic therapy (waxing, bleaching)</li>
<li>Induction of ovulation with anti-oestrogens (clomiphene, tamoxifen) and gonadotropins</li>
<li>Anti-DM meds; metformin</li>
<li><strong>Advise on high risk of dev'pt of type II DM, gestational DM, arterial disease like HT (androgen), endometrial hyperplasia &amp; CA</strong></li>
</ul>
<p>Mnx of pcos</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="oligomenorrhoea-amenorrhoea">Oligomenorrhoea/amenorrhoea<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#oligomenorrhoea-amenorrhoea" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>tend to be anovulatory, normal or high oestrogen levels.</li>
<li>endometrium that develops under the influence of oestrogen eventually becomes unsustainable and sheds.</li>
<li>For these reasons, cyclical progesterone is often useful in the treatment</li>
<li>Medroxyprogesterone acetate 10 mg daily for 10 days. The woman will normally bleed a few days after progesterone treatment stops.</li>
<li>metformin, increases insulin sensitivity, is partially effective in its treatment.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hirsutism">Hirsutism<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hirsutism" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>arises from the growth-promoting effects of androgen at the hair follicle.</li>
<li>Some of these growth-promoting effects are irreversible, even when androgen levels fall.</li>
<li>However, lowering free androgen levels will slow the rate of hair growth, which most patients see as a benefit.</li>
<li>The possible treatment options include the following.</li>
<li>Eflornithine cream, applied topically.</li>
<li>Cyproterone acetate: an anti-androgen that competitively inhibits the androgen receptor.</li>
<li>GnRH analogues with low-dose HRT: this regime should be reserved for women intolerant to other therapies, or for short-term treatment, since bone loss is an inevitable side effect.</li>
<li>Surgical treatments aimed at destroying the hair follicle, such as laser or electrolysis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="subfertility">Subfertility<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#subfertility" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>may respond to treatment either with clomiphene or with gonadotrophin therapy.</li>
<li>there is some evidence that metformin may increase ovulation rates, either alone or when used in combination with clomiphene.</li>
<li>metformin has been shown to increase ovulation rates (and therefore frequency of menses) by around once every 5 months.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="abnormal-uterine-bleeding-aub-figo-acog-2011">ABNORMAL UTERINE BLEEDING (AUB) (FIGO, ACOG-2011)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#abnormal-uterine-bleeding-aub-figo-acog-2011" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Any uterine bleeding outside the normal volume, duration, regularity or frequency is considered abnormal uterine bleeding (AUB).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="normal-menstruation">NORMAL MENSTRUATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#normal-menstruation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Cycle interval <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>28</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">=28</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.3669em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">28</span></span></span></span></span> days (21-35 days)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Menstrual flow <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>4</mn><mo>âˆ’</mo><mn>5</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">=4-5</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.3669em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">4</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">âˆ’</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">5</span></span></span></span></span> days</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Menstrual blood loss <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>35</mn><mrow><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">L</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>20</mn><mo>âˆ’</mo><mn>80</mn><mrow><mtext>&nbsp;</mtext><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">L</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">=35 \mathrm{~mL}(20-80 \mathrm{~mL})</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.3669em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">35</span><span class="mord"><span class="mspace nobreak">&nbsp;</span><span class="mord mathrm">mL</span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">20</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">âˆ’</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">80</span><span class="mord"><span class="mspace nobreak">&nbsp;</span><span class="mord mathrm">mL</span></span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Abnormal menstrual bleeding pattern have been traditionally expressed by terms like menorrhagia, metrorrhagia, polymenorrhea, and oligomenorrhea</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In order to create an universally accepted nomenclature to describe abnormal uterine bleeding, International Federation of Gynecology and Obstetrics (FIGO) and American College of Obstetricians and Gynaecologists (ACOG) introduced newer system of terminology to describe AUB.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The newer classification system is known by the acronym PALM-COEIN (FIGO-2011).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It is used to classify the abnormal uterine bleeding on the basis of etiology:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Polyp,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Adenomyosis,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Leiomyoma,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Malignancy and hyperplasia,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Coagulopathy,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ovulatory dysfunction,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Endometrial,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>latrogenic, and</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Not yet classified are the different etiological factors expressed by one (or more) letters.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="etiopathology-of-aub">Etiopathology of AUB<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#etiopathology-of-aub" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Structural causes (PALM)</p>
<ul>
<li>Polyp</li>
<li>Adenomyosis</li>
<li>Leiomyoma</li>
<li>Malignancy and hyperplasia</li>
</ul>
<p>Nonstructural systemic causes (COEIN)</p>
<ul>
<li>Coagulopathy</li>
<li>Ovulatory dysfunction</li>
<li>Endometrial</li>
<li>latrogenic</li>
<li>Not yet identified</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis-of-abnormal-uterine-bleeding">Diagnosis of Abnormal Uterine Bleeding<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis-of-abnormal-uterine-bleeding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Detailed history taking and physical examination</li>
</ul>
<p>History: Age,patterns of abnormal uterine bleeding, severity, associated pain, family history and use of medication</p>
<p>physical examination: Pallor, edema, neck glands, thyroid, and systemic examination, and pelvic examination (per speculum, Pap smear, and bimanual examination) are included</p>
<ul>
<li>Laboratory investigations: Complete hemogram, thyroid profile, pregnancy test, coagulation profile.</li>
<li>Imaging studies: Ultrasonography (Transvaginal), hysteroscopy</li>
<li>Magnetic resonance imaging (MRI): second line procedure especially in cases with adenomyosis.
E. Histological confirmation of pathology</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="postmenopausal-bleeding">POSTMENOPAUSAL BLEEDING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#postmenopausal-bleeding" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Vaginal bleeding after the menopause.</li>
<li>In women who are not taking HRT, any bleeding is abnormal.</li>
<li>In women on combined cyclical HRT, bleeding in the progesterone free period is normal.</li>
<li>Unscheduled bleeding refers to bleeding at other times, and this is abnormal and should be investigated.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aetiology-of-pmb">AETIOLOGY OF PMB<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aetiology-of-pmb" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>majority of women have atrophic vaginitis, whereby the vaginal epithelium thins and breaks down in response to low oestrogen levels.</li>
<li>This is a benign condition, which is relatively easily treated with topical oestrogens.</li>
<li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>10</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">10 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">10%</span></span></span></span></span> of women with PMB will be found to have endometrial cancer, the risk of which is greater for those who are not currently taking HRT, and progressively increases with increasing age.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="differential-diagnosis-of-pmb">Differential diagnosis OF PMB<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#differential-diagnosis-of-pmb" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>endometrial carcinoma</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>endometrial hyperplasia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>endometrial polyps</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>cervical malignancy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>atrophic vaginitis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Summary</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>AUB</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>â‹…</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\cdot</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">â‹…</span></span></span></span></span>In order to create an universally accepted nomenclature to describe abnormal uterine bleeding, International Federation of Gynecology and Obstetrics (FIGO) and American College of Obstetricians and Gynaecologists (ACOG) introduced newer system of terminology to describe AUB.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>â‹…</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\cdot</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">â‹…</span></span></span></span></span>The newer classification system is known by the acronym PALM-COEIN (FIGO-2011).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>â‹…</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\cdot</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.4445em;"></span><span class="mord">â‹…</span></span></span></span></span>It is used to classify the abnormal uterine bleeding on the basis of etiology:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>-Polyp,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>-Adenomyosis,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>-Leiomyoma,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>-Malignancy and hyperplasia,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>-Coagulopathy,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>-0vulatory dysfunction,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>-Endometrial,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>-latrogenic, and</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>-Not yet classified are the different etiological factors expressed by one (or more) letters.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="endometriosis">ENDOMETRIOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#endometriosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition">DEFINITION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="endometriosis">ENDOMETRIOSIS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#endometriosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Abnormal growths of tissue histologically resembling the endometrium in locations other than the uterine lining.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adenomyosis">ADENOMYOSIS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adenomyosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>n Presence of endometrial glands and stroma within the myometrium on hitological examination.</li>
<li>n Also called endometriosis interna</li>
<li>n ENDOMETRIOSIS</li>
<li>n It is a benign but it is locally invasive</li>
<li>n disseminates widely.</li>
<li>n Cyclic hormones stimulate growth</li>
<li>n Does NOT Discriminate by Race</li>
<li>n The prevalence is about 10 percent.
sites of endometriosis</li>
<li>Abdominal</li>
<li>Extra-abdominal:</li>
<li>
<div data-testid="stMarkdownPre" class="st-emotion-cache-acwcvw e1icttdg5"><div class="stCode st-emotion-cache-6ml83 e1xss9yb4" data-testid="stCode"><pre class="st-emotion-cache-1nqbjoj e1xss9yb2"><div style="background-color: transparent;"><code style="white-space: pre;"><span>- The common sites are abdominal scar of hysterotomy, cesarean section, tubectomy and myomectomy, umbilicus, episiotomy scar, vagina and cervix.</span></code></div></pre><div class="st-emotion-cache-chk1w8 e1xss9yb3"><button data-testid="stCodeCopyButton" title="Copy to clipboard" data-clipboard-text="- The common sites are abdominal scar of hysterotomy, cesarean section, tubectomy and myomectomy, umbilicus, episiotomy scar, vagina and cervix." style="top: 0px; right: 0px;" class="st-emotion-cache-1lyayqq e1xss9yb5"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><rect x="9" y="9" width="13" height="13" rx="2" ry="2"></rect><path d="M5 15H4a2 2 0 0 1-2-2V4a2 2 0 0 1 2-2h9a2 2 0 0 1 2 2v1"></path></svg></button></div></div></div>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="commonest-sites">Commonest sites<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#commonest-sites" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Ovary-50%. Pod, utero-sacral ligaments, posterior visceral surface of the uterus,broad ligament, bowel,bladder&amp;ureters.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rare - deep in the cervix,vaginal fornices,wounds contaminated with endometrial tissue.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Distant - out of the pelvis- lungs,brain&amp;kidney.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Risk factors</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Single/nulliparous</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Early menarche</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Non oral contraception</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Non smoker shorter cycle/longer duration of flow</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathogenesis">PATHOGENESIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathogenesis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>still remains unclear and is full of theories:</li>
<li>
<ol>
<li>Retrograde Menstruation (Sampson's theory):</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>There is retrograde flow of menstrual blood through the uterine tubes. Endometrial fragments get implanted in the peritoneal surface of the pelvic organs.</li>
<li>
<ol start="2">
<li>Coelomic metaplasia (Meyer and Ivanoff):</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>Chronic irritation of the pelvic peritoneum by the menstrual blood may cause coelomic metaplasia which results in endometriosis.</li>
<li>
<ol start="3">
<li>Lymphatic Theory (Halban):</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>
<div data-testid="stMarkdownPre" class="st-emotion-cache-acwcvw e1icttdg5"><div class="stCode st-emotion-cache-6ml83 e1xss9yb4" data-testid="stCode"><pre class="st-emotion-cache-1nqbjoj e1xss9yb2"><div style="background-color: transparent;"><code style="white-space: pre;"><span>- It may be possible for the normal endometrium to metastasize the pelvic lymph nodes through the draining lymphatic channels</span></code></div></pre><div class="st-emotion-cache-chk1w8 e1xss9yb3"><button data-testid="stCodeCopyButton" title="Copy to clipboard" data-clipboard-text="- It may be possible for the normal endometrium to metastasize the pelvic lymph nodes through the draining lymphatic channels" style="top: 0px; right: 0px;" class="st-emotion-cache-1lyayqq e1xss9yb5"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><rect x="9" y="9" width="13" height="13" rx="2" ry="2"></rect><path d="M5 15H4a2 2 0 0 1-2-2V4a2 2 0 0 1 2-2h9a2 2 0 0 1 2 2v1"></path></svg></button></div></div></div>
</li>
<li>
<ol start="4">
<li>Vascular Theory:</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>This is sound at least to explain endometriosis at distant sites such as lungs, arms or thighs.</li>
<li>
<ol start="5">
<li>others: Genetic and Immunological Factors, Direct Implantation, Environment theory.</li>
</ol>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathology">PATHOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Endometrial lesions appear as red velvety implants on the peritoneal surface. Further growth gives them a cystic, darkblue or black appearance. Lesions may grow to 5-10 mm surrounded by extensive adhesions. In the ovaries the cysts may enlarge to several cm ; endometriomas or 'chocolate cysts'.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">CLINICAL FEATURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The age is <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>30</mn><mo>âˆ’</mo><mn>45</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">30-45</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">30</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">âˆ’</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">45</span></span></span></span></span>.</li>
<li>Infertility,</li>
<li>patients are mostly nulliparous</li>
<li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>25</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">25 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">25%</span></span></span></span></span> have no symptom</li>
<li>Dysmenorrhea (70%)</li>
<li>Menorrhagia</li>
<li>Dyspareunia</li>
<li>Chronic Pelvic Pain</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="other-symptoms">Other Symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>n Urinaryâ€”frequency, dysuria, back pain or even hematuria</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>n Sigmoid colon and rectumâ€”painful defecation (dyschezia), diarrhea, constipation, rectal bleeding or even melena</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>n Chronic fatigue, perimenstrual symptoms (bowel, bladder)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>n Hemoptysis (rarely), catamenial chest pain</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>n Surgical scars-cyclical pain and bleeding</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Diagnosis</p>
<ul>
<li>confirm by laparoscopy\laparotomy and biopsy for histology. ("Gold Standard)</li>
<li>Inconclusive Ix:</li>
<li>
<div data-testid="stMarkdownPre" class="st-emotion-cache-acwcvw e1icttdg5"><div class="stCode st-emotion-cache-6ml83 e1xss9yb4" data-testid="stCode"><pre class="st-emotion-cache-1nqbjoj e1xss9yb2"><div style="background-color: transparent;"><code style="white-space: pre;"><span>- CA-125 - moderate elevationin patients with severe endometriosis,</span></code></div></pre><div class="st-emotion-cache-chk1w8 e1xss9yb3"><button data-testid="stCodeCopyButton" title="Copy to clipboard" data-clipboard-text="- CA-125 - moderate elevationin patients with severe endometriosis," style="top: 0px; right: 0px;" class="st-emotion-cache-1lyayqq e1xss9yb5"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><rect x="9" y="9" width="13" height="13" rx="2" ry="2"></rect><path d="M5 15H4a2 2 0 0 1-2-2V4a2 2 0 0 1 2-2h9a2 2 0 0 1 2 2v1"></path></svg></button></div></div></div>
</li>
<li>
<div data-testid="stMarkdownPre" class="st-emotion-cache-acwcvw e1icttdg5"><div class="stCode st-emotion-cache-6ml83 e1xss9yb4" data-testid="stCode"><pre class="st-emotion-cache-1nqbjoj e1xss9yb2"><div style="background-color: transparent;"><code style="white-space: pre;"><span>- History \&amp; Pelvic Exam,</span></code></div></pre><div class="st-emotion-cache-chk1w8 e1xss9yb3"><button data-testid="stCodeCopyButton" title="Copy to clipboard" data-clipboard-text="- History \&amp; Pelvic Exam," style="top: 0px; right: 0px;" class="st-emotion-cache-1lyayqq e1xss9yb5"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><rect x="9" y="9" width="13" height="13" rx="2" ry="2"></rect><path d="M5 15H4a2 2 0 0 1-2-2V4a2 2 0 0 1 2-2h9a2 2 0 0 1 2 2v1"></path></svg></button></div></div></div>
</li>
<li>
<div data-testid="stMarkdownPre" class="st-emotion-cache-acwcvw e1icttdg5"><div class="stCode st-emotion-cache-6ml83 e1xss9yb4" data-testid="stCode"><pre class="st-emotion-cache-1nqbjoj e1xss9yb2"><div style="background-color: transparent;"><code style="white-space: pre;"><span>- Imaging Studies</span></code></div></pre><div class="st-emotion-cache-chk1w8 e1xss9yb3"><button data-testid="stCodeCopyButton" title="Copy to clipboard" data-clipboard-text="- Imaging Studies" style="top: 0px; right: 0px;" class="st-emotion-cache-1lyayqq e1xss9yb5"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><rect x="9" y="9" width="13" height="13" rx="2" ry="2"></rect><path d="M5 15H4a2 2 0 0 1-2-2V4a2 2 0 0 1 2-2h9a2 2 0 0 1 2 2v1"></path></svg></button></div></div></div>
</li>
<li>Ultrasonography is not much helpful to the diagnosis.</li>
<li>MRI &amp; CT scan</li>
</ul>
<p>Treatment: Overall Approach
Recognize Goals:</p>
<ul>
<li>Pain Management</li>
<li>Preservation / Restoration of Fertility</li>
</ul>
<p>Discuss with Patient:</p>
<ul>
<li>Disease may be Chronic and Not Curable</li>
<li>Optimal Treatment Unproven or Nonexistent</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="treatment">TREATMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Depends on desire for future fertility, symptoms, disease stage and age of the patient.</p>
<p>Minimal disease - observe on NSAIDS and prostaglandin inhibitors.
Moderate - pseudo pregnancy - ocps.
Severe disease - pseudomenopause - e.g.. Danazol, gnrh agonists - Buserelin , Goserelin, Leuprorelin .</p>
<p>Surgery - excision &amp; adhesionolysis, For those with DFS - TAH + BSO, Appendicectomy and excision of all lesions.</p>
<p>Pain Management: Medical Therapy</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>NSAIDs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>OCPs (Continuous)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Progestins</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Danazol</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>GnRH-a</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>GnRH-a + Add-Back Therapy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Misc: Opoids, TCAs, SSRIs</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="surgical-treatment">Surgical Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>(Laparoscopy / Laparotomy</li>
<li>Excision / Fulgeration</li>
<li>Resection of Endometrioma</li>
<li>Lysis of Adhesions, Cul-de-sac Reconstruction</li>
<li>Uterosacral Nerve Ablation</li>
<li>Presacral Neurectomy</li>
<li>Appendectomy</li>
<li>Uterine Suspension</li>
<li>Hysterectomy +/- BSO</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prognosis">PROGNOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prognosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Counseling after diagnosis and staging is vital for decision of management mode.</li>
<li>May reccur even after definitive surgery</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adenomyosis">ADENOMYOSIS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adenomyosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Adenomyosis is a condition where there is in-growth of the endometrium, both the glandular and stromal components, directly into the myometrium.</li>
<li>The cause of such in-growth is not known.</li>
<li>It may be related to repeated childbirths, vigorous curettage or excess of estrogen effect</li>
<li>It is thought to be direct contamination of endometrial surface where isolate islands have lost the connection with the surface endometrium from fibrosis or musculature.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">CLINICAL FEATURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>one-third remains asymptomatic</li>
<li>Menorrhagia (70%) - unresponsive to hormonal therapy or uterine curettage</li>
<li>Dysmenorrhea (30%)</li>
<li>Pelvic pain</li>
<li>Dyspareunia or frequency of urination</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="magnetic-resonance-imaging-mri">Magnetic Resonance Imaging (MRI)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#magnetic-resonance-imaging-mri" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>MRI should be expected to be excellent in recognizing uterine masses like fibroids, cysts, and adenomyomas if they reach 5 mm . or greater in size.</p>
<p>MRI may be able to lead us to expect adenomyosis if the myometrial thickness is increased or the consistency of the myometrium is changed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hysterography">Hysterography<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hysterography" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>the presence of ill defined areas of contrast intravasation extending perpendicularly from the uterine cavity into the myometrium is the most characteristic feature of adenomyosis on hysterography.</p>
<p>Unfortunately, the sensitivity of this technique is too low for clinical practice.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="n-treatment">n TREATMENT:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#n-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>n The only definitive treatment for adenomyosis is total hysterectomy, with or without ovarian conservation.
n Chemotherapy - ocps reduce pain and bleeding.
n DXT - destroys ovaries and reduces I.e. for those who cannot stand surgery.
n Prognosis - Hysterectomy is curative.
n Levonorgestrel-releasing-IUS is found to improve the menorrhagia and dysmenorrhea.
n Danazolâ€”loaded (300-400 mg) intrauterine device (IUD) is also found to improve the symptoms of menorrhagia and dysmenorrhea.</p>
<p>A good gynecologist may suspect adenomyosis based on the clinical factors, but the final diagnosis usually has to wait until hysterectomy is performed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="summary">Summary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="endometriosis">ENDOMETRIOSIS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#endometriosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Abnormal growths of tissue histologically resembling the endometrium in locations other than the uterine lining
Diagnosis: confirm by laparoscopy\laparotomy and biopsy for histology. ("Gold Standard) Treatment: Depends on desire for future fertility, symptoms, disease stage and age of the patient.</p>
<ul>
<li>Minimal disease - observe on NSAIDS and prostaglandin inhibitors.</li>
<li>Moderate - pseudo pregnancy - ocps.</li>
<li>Severe disease - pseudomenopause - e.g.. Danazol, gnrh agonists - Buserelin , Goserelin, Leuprorelin .</li>
<li>Surgery - excision &amp; adhesionolysis, For those with DFS - TAH + BSO, Appendicectomy and excision of all lesions.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adenomyosis">ADENOMYOSIS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adenomyosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Presence of endometrial glands and stroma within the myometrium on hitological examination.</p>
<p>Also called endometriosis interna
The only definitive treatment for adenomyosis is total hysterectomy, with or without ovarian conservation</p>
<p>A good gynecologist may suspect adenomyosis based on the clinical factors, but the final diagnosis usually has to wait until hysterectomy is performed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unit-five-content">Unit Five Content..<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-five-content" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="topic-1-fertilization-and-implantation">Topic 1: Fertilization and Implantation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#topic-1-fertilization-and-implantation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fertilization">FERTILIZATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fertilization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Fertilization is the process of fusion of the spermatozoon with the mature ovum. It begins with sperm egg collision and ends with production of a mononucleated single cell called the zygote. Its objectives are:</p>
<p>(1) To initiate the embryonic development of the egg and
(2) To restore the chromosome number of the species.</p>
<p>Almost always, fertilization occurs in the ampullary part of the uterine tube.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="process-of-fertilization">Process of Fertilization<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#process-of-fertilization" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>After the male ejaculates semen into the vagina during intercourse, a few sperm are transported within 5 to 10 minutes upward from the vagina and through the uterus and fallopian tubes to the
ampullae of the fallopian tubes near the ovarian ends of the tubes.
